Hudud — Fixed Penalties
advanced
8 min
Direct Denial of Necessarily Known Prohibitions (Istihlal) as Apostasy
Enumeration of statements and actions of istihlal that cause apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between legitimate interpretation (ta'wil) and outright denial that leads to kufr in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Deeming a necessarily known haram as halal (istihlal) is kufr; mere sin without istihlal is not.

The Hanafi jurists detail specific statements and acts that remove a person from the fold of Islam. A key category is istihlal—deeming something permissible that is definitively known to be forbidden from the religion. This lesson focuses on such cases, including denial of the prohibition of wine, sodomy, and intercourse during menstruation, highlighting the role of knowledge and intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act or statement
Read each scenario in the passage and determine whether the person denies a clear prohibition or merely commits a sin.
Not all sins are apostasy; the key is whether the person deems the sin permissible (istihlal).
2
Check the knowledge condition
See if the person is aware that the act is haram in the religion. If unaware or mistaken (e.g., due to ignorance), kufr may not apply.
The text qualifies: 'if he knows its prohibition from the religion'.
3
Determine if there is ta'wil (interpretation)
If the person had a plausible interpretation that the prohibition is not definitive, they may not become a disbeliever.
Example: deeming intercourse during menstruation permissible based on interpreting the prohibition as advisory, not absolute.
4
Apply the Hanafi ruling
Once istihlal of a necessarily known prohibition is confirmed, the person is judged a murtadd. Note any intra-Hanafi differences (e.g., regarding menstruation).
The text mentions the view of Imam al-Sarakhsi that it is kufr without detail.
5
Distinguish from mere sin
A person who commits a prohibited act while recognizing its prohibition is sinful but not a disbeliever.
This is a foundational distinction in Hanafi 'aqida and fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحرام، وقيده بعضهم بما إذا كان يعلم حرمتها لا بقوله الخمر حرام ولكن ليست هذه التي زعمون أنها حرام .، ويكفر من قال إن حرمة الخمر لم تثبت بالقرآن ومن زعم أن الصغائر والكبائر حلال، وباستحلاله الجماع للحائض لا في الاستبراء وقيل لا في الأول وهو الصحيح، ولا باستحلال سؤر كلب أو ريع أرض غصب وباستحلال اللواطة إن علم حرمته من الدين، حلال حين نهى عن تقبيله أجنبية، وبقوله الشريعة كلها تلبيس أو حيل إن قال وبقوله هي . لي في كل الشرائع لا فيما يرجع إلى المعاملات مما تصح فيه الحيل الشرعية وقيل يكفر في الأول مطلقاً ويخاف عليه الكفر إذا شتم عالماً أو فقيهاً من غير سبب، ويكفر بقوله لعالم ذكر الحمار في أست علمك مريداً به علم الدين، وبجلوسه على مكان مرتفع والتشبه بالمذكرين ومع جماعة يسألون منه المسائل ويضحكون منه ثم يضربونه بالمحراق، وكذا يكفر الجميع لاستخفافهم بالشرع، وكذا لو لم يجلس على مكان مرتفع ولكن يستهزئ بالمذكرين ويتمشى والقوم يضحكون، وبإلقاء الفتوى على الأرض حين أتى بها خصمه، وبقوله لا تذهب وإن ذهبت تطلق امرأتك استهزاء بالعلم والعلماء جواباً لمن قال إلى مجلس العلم جواباً لقوله أين تذهب، وبقوله قصعة من تريد خير من العلم لا بقوله خير من الله لإرادته أنها نعمة والأول لا تأويل له سوى الاستخفاف بالعلم، وبقول المريض المشتد مرضه إن شئت توفني مسلماً وإن شئت كافراً، وبقول المبتلي أخذت مالي وأحذت ولدي وأخذت كذا وكذا فماذا تفعل وماذا بقي وبقوله عمداً لا جواباً لمن قال له ألست مسلماً حين ضرب عبده أو ولده ضرباً شديداً إلا إن غلط أو قصد الجواب وبقول الزوج ليس لي حمية ولا دين الإسلام حين قالت له امرأته ذلك، وبقوله لمسلم يا كافر عند البعض ولو أحد الزوجين للآخر والمختار للفتوى أن يكفر إن اعتقده كافراً لا إن أراد شتمه وبقوله لبيك جواباً لمن قال يا كافر يا يهودي يا مجوسي، وبقوله أنا ملحد لأن الملحد كافر ولو قال ما علمته لا يعذر، وبقول المعتذر لغيره كنت كافراً فأسلمت عند بعضهم وقيل لا، وبقوله كنت مجوسياً أسلمت الآن، وبنسيان العاصي التوبة وتحقير الذنب وعدم رؤية العقوبة بالذنب وعدم رؤية المعاصي قبيحة الطاعات ، وبعدم رؤية الطاعة حسناً وبعدم رؤيته الثواب على الطاعة وبعدم رؤيته وجوب من الله الاستبراء بدعة وضلال وليس بكفر وعن إبراهيم بن رستم أنه قال : إن استحل الجماع في الحيض متأولاً أن النهي ليس للتحريم أو لم يعرف النهي لم يكفر، وإن عرف النهي واعتقد أن النهي للتحريم ذلك استحل كان كافراً. وعن شمس الأئمة السرخسي أن استحلال الجماع في الحيض كفر من غير تفصيل . قوله : ( وبنسيان العاصي التوبة إلى قوله وبعدم رؤيته الطاعة حسناء) أي يكفر برؤيته مجموع وبقوله كفرت حين تكلم بكلمة زعم القوم أنها كفر وليست بكفر فقيل له كفرت وطلقت زوجتك، وتكفر المرأة إذا تكلمت بالكفر لقصد أن تحرم على زوجها والإيمان مستقر في قلبها، وقولها أصير كافرة حتى أتخلص من الزوج، ومن قصد الكفر ساعة أو يوماً فهو كافر في جميع العمر، وبتمنيه الكفر أن لو كان كافراً فأسلم حين أسلم كافراً فأعطي شيئاً، وبتمنيه أن لم يحرم الظلم والزنا والقتل بغير حق وكل حرام لا يكون حلالاً في وقت بخلاف الخمر ومناكحة المحارم، وبتمنيه أن لو كان نصرانياً حتى يتزوج نصرانية سمينة رآها، وبوضع قلنسوة المجوسي على رأسه على الصحيح إلا لضرورة دفع الحر أو البرد، وبشد الزنار في وسطه إلا إذا فعل ذلك خديعة في الحرب وطليعة للمسلمين وبقول معلم صبيان اليهود خير من المسلمين بكثير فإنهم يقضون حقوق معلمي صبيانهم وبقوله المجوسية خير مما أنا فيه يعني فعله، وبقوله النصرانية خير من المجوسية لا بقوله المجوسية شر من النصرانية، وبقوله النصرانية خير من اليهودية وينبغي أن يقول النصرانية شر من اليهودية، وبقوله لمعاملة الكفر خير مما أنت تفعل عند بعضهم مطلقاً، وقيده الفقيه أبو الليث بأن يقصد تحسين الكفر لا تقبيح معاملته، وبخروجه إلى نيروز المجوس والموافقة معهم فيما يفعلون في ذلك اليوم النيروز شيئاً لم يكن يشتريه قبل ذلك تعظيماً للنيروز لا للأكل والشرب وبإهدائه ذلك اليوم للمشركين ولو بيضة تعظيماً لذلك اليوم لا بإجابته دعوة مجوسي حلق رأس ولده وبتحسين أمر الكفار اتفاقاً . حتى قالوا: لو قال ترك الكلام عند أكل الطعام من المجوسي أو ترك المضاجعة حالة الحيض منهم حسن فهو كافر. وبذبحه شيئاً في وجه إنسان وقت الخلعة أو للقادم من الحج أو الغزو والمذبوح ميتة وقيل لا يكفر، وقوله لسلطان زماننا عادل وقيل لا وعلى هذا الاختلاف قول الخطباء في ألقاب السلطان العادل الأعظم مالك رقاب الأمم سلطان أرض الله مالك بلاد الله، وبقوله لا تقل للسلطان هذا حين عطس السلطان فقال له رجل يرحمك الله، وبسقي ولده الخمر فجاء أقرباؤه ونثروا الدراهم والسكر كفر الكل، وكذا لو لم ينثروا الدراهم ولكنهم قالوا مبارك، واختلفوا فيما إذا قال أحب الخمر فلا أصبر عنها . ويكفر بتلقين كلمة الكفر ليتكلم بها ولو على وجه اللعب وبأمره امرأة بالارتداد لتبين من زوجها، وبالإفتاء بذلك وإن لم تكفر المرأة بناء على أن الرضا بكفر غيره كفر وقيل لا، ذلك ولذا لم يكرر حرف الجر. قوله : (بناء على الرضا بكفر غيره كفر قال في التتارخانية : وفي النصاب الأصح أنه لا يكفر بالرضا بكفر الغير. وفي غرر المعاني : لا خلاف بين مشايخنا أن الأمر بالكفر كفر. وفي شرح السير : إن الرضا بكفر الغير إنما يكون كفراً إذا كان يستخف الكفر ويستحسنه أما إذا أحب الموت أو القتل على الكفر لمن كان شديداً مؤذياً بطبعه حتى ينتقم الله تعالى
With haram, and some qualified it as when he knows its prohibition, not by his saying 'wine is haram' but it is not this which they claim is haram. And he becomes a disbeliever who says that the prohibition of wine is not established by the Quran, and who claims that minor and major sins are permissible. And by his deeming permissible intercourse with a menstruating woman, not during istibra', and it is said not in the first, and that is correct. And not by deeming permissible the leftover of a dog or the rent of usurped land. And by deeming permissible sodomy if he knows its prohibition from the religion. And by his saying 'the entire sharia is deception or tricks' if he says, and by his saying 'it is for me in all laws, not in what relates to transactions where legal tricks are valid'; and it is said he disbelieves in the first absolutely. And he is feared for disbelief if he insults a scholar or jurist without cause. And he disbelieves by his saying to a scholar 'mention the donkey in the anus of your knowledge' intending thereby religious knowledge. And by his sitting in an elevated place and imitating the preachers, and with a group asking him questions and laughing at him, then they strike him with a firebrand; likewise all disbelieve for their mockery of the law. Likewise if he did not sit in an elevated place but mocks the preachers and walks while the people laugh. And by throwing the fatwa on the ground when his opponent brought it. And by his saying 'don't go, and if you go your wife is divorced' as mockery of knowledge and scholars, in response to one who said 'to the assembly of knowledge', in answer to his saying 'where are you going?' And by his saying 'a bowl of what you want is better than knowledge', not by his saying 'better than Allah' because he intends it as a blessing, and the first has no interpretation except mockery of knowledge. And by the sick person in severe illness saying 'if You wish, cause me to die as a Muslim, and if You wish, as a disbeliever.' And by the afflicted saying 'You took my wealth and took my child and took such and such, so what do You do and what remains?' and by his saying it intentionally, not in response to one who said to him 'Are you not a Muslim?' when he severely beat his slave or child, unless he made a mistake or intended the answer. And by the husband saying 'I have no zeal nor the religion of Islam' when his wife said that to him. And by his saying to a Muslim 'O disbeliever' according to some, even if one of the spouses to the other; and the chosen for fatwa is that he disbelieves if he believes him to be a disbeliever, not if he intended insult. And by his saying 'labayk' in response to one who said 'O disbeliever, O Jew, O Magian.' And by his saying 'I am an atheist' because the atheist is a disbeliever; and if he said 'I did not know it' he is not excused. And by the one apologizing to another saying 'I was a disbeliever and then became Muslim' according to some, and it is said no. And by his saying 'I was a Magian and now I accept Islam.' And by the sinner forgetting repentance, belittling sin, not seeing punishment for sin, and not seeing sins as ugly and acts of obedience as good, and not seeing obedience as good, and not seeing reward for obedience, and not seeing the obligation from Allah... Istibra' is innovation and misguidance, not disbelief. And from Ibrahim ibn Rustam that he said: If he deems permissible intercourse during menstruation interpreting that the prohibition is not for prohibition or if he did not know the prohibition, he does not disbelieve; and if he knew the prohibition and believed the prohibition is for prohibition and then deemed it permissible, he becomes a disbeliever. And from Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi that deeming permissible intercourse during menstruation is disbelief without detail. His statement: (And by the sinner forgetting repentance until his statement: and by his not seeing obedience as good) meaning he disbelieves by seeing the totality... And by his saying 'I disbelieved' when he spoke a word that the people claimed is disbelief but it is not disbelief, so it was said to him 'you disbelieved and your wife is divorced.' And a woman disbelieves if she speaks disbelief with the intention that she become forbidden to her husband while faith is settled in her heart, and her saying 'I become a disbeliever so that I get rid of my husband.' And whoever intends disbelief for an hour or a day is a disbeliever for all his life. And by his wishing for disbelief, that if he were a disbeliever and then became Muslim when he became Muslim as a disbeliever, so he was given something. And by his wishing that injustice, adultery, and murder without right were not prohibited, and every prohibited thing that is not permissible at any time, unlike wine and marrying mahrams. And by his wishing that he were a Christian so he could marry a fat Christian woman he saw. And by placing a Magian cap on his head, according to the correct view, except for necessity to repel heat or cold. And by tying a zunnar around his waist, except if he does it as a trick in war and as a lookout for Muslims. And by the statement of the teacher of Jewish children: 'They are much better than Muslims' because they fulfill the rights of their teachers, and by his saying 'Magianism is better than what I am in', meaning his action. And by his saying 'Christianity is better than Magianism', not by his saying 'Magianism is worse than Christianity.' And by his saying 'Christianity is better than Judaism'; it is proper that he say 'Christianity is worse than Judaism.' And by his saying 'The transaction of disbelief is better than what you do' according to some absolutely; and Abu al-Layth qualified it as intending to beautify disbelief, not to disparage his transaction. And by his going out to the Persian New Year (Nawruz) and agreeing with them in what they do on that day of Nawruz, buying something he did not buy before, to venerate Nawruz not for eating and drinking. And by his gifting on that day to the polytheists even an egg, to venerate that day, not by his accepting an invitation from a Magian who shaved his son's head. And by beautifying the affairs of the disbelievers unanimously; until they said: if he said 'remaining silent during eating from the Magian' or 'not lying with a menstruating woman from them is good', then he is a disbeliever. And by his slaughtering something in front of a person at the time of khil'a or for the one arriving from Hajj or battle, and the slaughtered animal is carrion; and it is said he does not disbelieve. And his saying 'Our present ruler is just'; and it is said no; and upon this difference is the statement of the orators in the titles 'the just greatest sultan, owner of the necks of the nations, sultan of Allah's earth, owner of Allah's lands.' And by his saying 'Do not say to the sultan this' when the sultan sneezed and a man said to him 'May Allah have mercy on you.' And by his giving his child wine to drink, then his relatives came and scattered dirhams and sugar, all disbelieve; likewise if they did not scatter dirhams but said 'blessed.' And they differed regarding if he said 'I love wine and cannot abstain from it.' And he disbelieves by prompting a word of disbelief for him to speak, even if in jest. And by his ordering a woman to apostatize so she becomes separated from her husband, and by issuing a fatwa to that effect, even if the woman does not disbelieve, based on the principle that being pleased with another's disbelief is disbelief; and it is said no. That is why the preposition is not repeated. His statement: (based on the principle that being pleased with another's disbelief is disbelief) as stated in al-Tatarkhaniyya: and in al-Nisab the correct is that he does not disbelieve by being pleased with another's disbelief. And in Ghurar al-Ma'ani: there is no disagreement among our scholars that commanding disbelief is disbelief. And in Sharh al-Siyar: being pleased with another's disbelief is only disbelief if he mocks disbelief and considers it good; but if he loves death or killing on disbelief for someone who is severely harmful by nature so that Allah takes vengeance...
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an extensive enumeration of statements and actions that, according to the Hanafi school, render a Muslim an apostate (murtadd). The text covers a wide range of scenarios, from direct denial of established prohibitions (like wine) to mockery of scholars and religious knowledge, to specific actions such as wearing a Magian cap or participating in non-Islamic festivals. The author often notes differences of opinion (e.g., 'qila' or 'ind ba'dihim') and occasionally provides tarjih (preferred view). The underlying principle is that any explicit rejection of a necessarily known tenet of Islam, or any act that clearly indicates contempt for the religion, constitutes kufr. The text also addresses nuances, such as when a statement is made in jest or out of ignorance, and the importance of intent. The final part discusses the controversial issue of being pleased with another's disbelief (rida bi kufr al-ghayr) and notes that commanding kufr is definitely kufr, but mere approval may not be, according to some authorities. This passage serves as a practical guide for judges and jurists in identifying apostasy.

Key Terms
استحلال (istihlal): Deeming something prohibited to be permissible; a major cause of apostasy if the prohibition is necessarily known from the religion.
المحرمات المعلومة من الدين بالضرورة (al-muharramat al-ma'luma min al-din bi al-darura): Prohibitions that every Muslim knows are part of the religion, e.g., zina, riba, khamr. Denying them can lead to kufr.
تأويل (ta'wil): Interpretation that allows a different understanding of a text; can prevent the ruling of kufr if plausible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the lesson, why is deeming permissible the leftover of a dog not considered kufr?
A) Because the prohibition of dog saliva is not necessarily known from the religion.
B) Because dogs are impure but their saliva is pure.
C) Because it is permissible to use dog saliva in medicine.
D) Because the Hanafi school does not consider dogs impure.

Key Takeaway
Istihlal of a necessarily known prohibition is kufr; the key factors are knowledge of the prohibition and deliberate justification of its permissibility.

8 min
Mockery of Scholars, Knowledge, and Religion as Apostasy
Enumeration of mocking statements and actions that cause apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify statements and actions that constitute mockery (istikhfaf) of religion and thus cause apostasy according to Hanafi jurists.

Core Idea
Mocking any element of the religion, even if done in jest, is kufr.

The Hanafi jurists list numerous actions and statements that indicate contempt for religious knowledge, scholars, or the sharia itself. These range from insulting a scholar to throwing a fatwa on the ground, or saying religious knowledge is worthless. This lesson explores the principle that any act of mockery (istikhfaf) of the religion removes one from Islam, regardless of intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of mockery
Determine whether the act targets a scholar, a religious ruling, or the sharia itself.
The text includes insults to a scholar, mockery of preachers, and statements belittling knowledge.
2
Assess the manner
Was the statement serious or in jest? Note that jest does not excuse; in fact, jesting about religion is worse.
The text says 'ولو على وجه اللعب' (even in play) is still kufr.
3
Distinguish from legitimate criticism
Criticism of individual scholars for valid reasons may not be kufr, but mockery of the office or knowledge is.
Insulting a scholar 'without cause' is feared for kufr; with a valid reason, it may be fisq.
4
Apply the ruling
Once mockery is established, the person is judged a murtadd, unless they had a valid excuse (e.g., mistake).
Exceptions are rare; the default is kufr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بحرام، وقيده بعضهم بما إذا كان يعلم حرمتها لا بقوله الخمر حرام ولكن ليست هذه التي زعمون أنها حرام .، ويكفر من قال إن حرمة الخمر لم تثبت بالقرآن ومن زعم أن الصغائر والكبائر حلال، وباستحلاله الجماع للحائض لا في الاستبراء وقيل لا في الأول وهو الصحيح، ولا باستحلال سؤر كلب أو ريع أرض غصب وباستحلال اللواطة إن علم حرمته من الدين، حلال حين نهى عن تقبيله أجنبية، وبقوله الشريعة كلها تلبيس أو حيل إن قال وبقوله هي . لي في كل الشرائع لا فيما يرجع إلى المعاملات مما تصح فيه الحيل الشرعية وقيل يكفر في الأول مطلقاً ويخاف عليه الكفر إذا شتم عالماً أو فقيهاً من غير سبب، ويكفر بقوله لعالم ذكر الحمار في أست علمك مريداً به علم الدين، وبجلوسه على مكان مرتفع والتشبه بالمذكرين ومع جماعة يسألون منه المسائل ويضحكون منه ثم يضربونه بالمحراق، وكذا يكفر الجميع لاستخفافهم بالشرع، وكذا لو لم يجلس على مكان مرتفع ولكن يستهزئ بالمذكرين ويتمشى والقوم يضحكون، وبإلقاء الفتوى على الأرض حين أتى بها خصمه، وبقوله لا تذهب وإن ذهبت تطلق امرأتك استهزاء بالعلم والعلماء جواباً لمن قال إلى مجلس العلم جواباً لقوله أين تذهب، وبقوله قصعة من تريد خير من العلم لا بقوله خير من الله لإرادته أنها نعمة والأول لا تأويل له سوى الاستخفاف بالعلم، وبقول المريض المشتد مرضه إن شئت توفني مسلماً وإن شئت كافراً، وبقول المبتلي أخذت مالي وأحذت ولدي وأخذت كذا وكذا فماذا تفعل وماذا بقي وبقوله عمداً لا جواباً لمن قال له ألست مسلماً حين ضرب عبده أو ولده ضرباً شديداً إلا إن غلط أو قصد الجواب وبقول الزوج ليس لي حمية ولا دين الإسلام حين قالت له امرأته ذلك، وبقوله لمسلم يا كافر عند البعض ولو أحد الزوجين للآخر والمختار للفتوى أن يكفر إن اعتقده كافراً لا إن أراد شتمه وبقوله لبيك جواباً لمن قال يا كافر يا يهودي يا مجوسي، وبقوله أنا ملحد لأن الملحد كافر ولو قال ما علمته لا يعذر، وبقول المعتذر لغيره كنت كافراً فأسلمت عند بعضهم وقيل لا، وبقوله كنت مجوسياً أسلمت الآن، وبنسيان العاصي التوبة وتحقير الذنب وعدم رؤية العقوبة بالذنب وعدم رؤية المعاصي قبيحة الطاعات ، وبعدم رؤية الطاعة حسناً وبعدم رؤيته الثواب على الطاعة وبعدم رؤيته وجوب من الله الاستبراء بدعة وضلال وليس بكفر وعن إبراهيم بن رستم أنه قال : إن استحل الجماع في الحيض متأولاً أن النهي ليس للتحريم أو لم يعرف النهي لم يكفر، وإن عرف النهي واعتقد أن النهي للتحريم ذلك استحل كان كافراً. وعن شمس الأئمة السرخسي أن استحلال الجماع في الحيض كفر من غير تفصيل . قوله : ( وبنسيان العاصي التوبة إلى قوله وبعدم رؤيته الطاعة حسناء) أي يكفر برؤيته مجموع وبقوله كفرت حين تكلم بكلمة زعم القوم أنها كفر وليست بكفر فقيل له كفرت وطلقت زوجتك، وتكفر المرأة إذا تكلمت بالكفر لقصد أن تحرم على زوجها والإيمان مستقر في قلبها، وقولها أصير كافرة حتى أتخلص من الزوج، ومن قصد الكفر ساعة أو يوماً فهو كافر في جميع العمر، وبتمنيه الكفر أن لو كان كافراً فأسلم حين أسلم كافراً فأعطي شيئاً، وبتمنيه أن لم يحرم الظلم والزنا والقتل بغير حق وكل حرام لا يكون حلالاً في وقت بخلاف الخمر ومناكحة المحارم، وبتمنيه أن لو كان نصرانياً حتى يتزوج نصرانية سمينة رآها، وبوضع قلنسوة المجوسي على رأسه على الصحيح إلا لضرورة دفع الحر أو البرد، وبشد الزنار في وسطه إلا إذا فعل ذلك خديعة في الحرب وطليعة للمسلمين وبقول معلم صبيان اليهود خير من المسلمين بكثير فإنهم يقضون حقوق معلمي صبيانهم وبقوله المجوسية خير مما أنا فيه يعني فعله، وبقوله النصرانية خير من المجوسية لا بقوله المجوسية شر من النصرانية، وبقوله النصرانية خير من اليهودية وينبغي أن يقول النصرانية شر من اليهودية، وبقوله لمعاملة الكفر خير مما أنت تفعل عند بعضهم مطلقاً، وقيده الفقيه أبو الليث بأن يقصد تحسين الكفر لا تقبيح معاملته، وبخروجه إلى نيروز المجوس والموافقة معهم فيما يفعلون في ذلك اليوم النيروز شيئاً لم يكن يشتريه قبل ذلك تعظيماً للنيروز لا للأكل والشرب وبإهدائه ذلك اليوم للمشركين ولو بيضة تعظيماً لذلك اليوم لا بإجابته دعوة مجوسي حلق رأس ولده وبتحسين أمر الكفار اتفاقاً . حتى قالوا: لو قال ترك الكلام عند أكل الطعام من المجوسي أو ترك المضاجعة حالة الحيض منهم حسن فهو كافر. وبذبحه شيئاً في وجه إنسان وقت الخلعة أو للقادم من الحج أو الغزو والمذبوح ميتة وقيل لا يكفر، وقوله لسلطان زماننا عادل وقيل لا وعلى هذا الاختلاف قول الخطباء في ألقاب السلطان العادل الأعظم مالك رقاب الأمم سلطان أرض الله مالك بلاد الله، وبقوله لا تقل للسلطان هذا حين عطس السلطان فقال له رجل يرحمك الله، وبسقي ولده الخمر فجاء أقرباؤه ونثروا الدراهم والسكر كفر الكل، وكذا لو لم ينثروا الدراهم ولكنهم قالوا مبارك، واختلفوا فيما إذا قال أحب الخمر فلا أصبر عنها . ويكفر بتلقين كلمة الكفر ليتكلم بها ولو على وجه اللعب وبأمره امرأة بالارتداد لتبين من زوجها، وبالإفتاء بذلك وإن لم تكفر المرأة بناء على أن الرضا بكفر غيره كفر وقيل لا، ذلك ولذا لم يكرر حرف الجر. قوله : (بناء على الرضا بكفر غيره كفر قال في التتارخانية : وفي النصاب الأصح أنه لا يكفر بالرضا بكفر الغير. وفي غرر المعاني : لا خلاف بين مشايخنا أن الأمر بالكفر كفر. وفي شرح السير : إن الرضا بكفر الغير إنما يكون كفراً إذا كان يستخف الكفر ويستحسنه أما إذا أحب الموت أو القتل على الكفر لمن كان شديداً مؤذياً بطبعه حتى ينتقم الله تعالى
With haram, and some qualified it as when he knows its prohibition, not by his saying 'wine is haram' but it is not this which they claim is haram. And he becomes a disbeliever who says that the prohibition of wine is not established by the Quran, and who claims that minor and major sins are permissible. And by his deeming permissible intercourse with a menstruating woman, not during istibra', and it is said not in the first, and that is correct. And not by deeming permissible the leftover of a dog or the rent of usurped land. And by deeming permissible sodomy if he knows its prohibition from the religion. And by his saying 'the entire sharia is deception or tricks' if he says, and by his saying 'it is for me in all laws, not in what relates to transactions where legal tricks are valid'; and it is said he disbelieves in the first absolutely. And he is feared for disbelief if he insults a scholar or jurist without cause. And he disbelieves by his saying to a scholar 'mention the donkey in the anus of your knowledge' intending thereby religious knowledge. And by his sitting in an elevated place and imitating the preachers, and with a group asking him questions and laughing at him, then they strike him with a firebrand; likewise all disbelieve for their mockery of the law. Likewise if he did not sit in an elevated place but mocks the preachers and walks while the people laugh. And by throwing the fatwa on the ground when his opponent brought it. And by his saying 'don't go, and if you go your wife is divorced' as mockery of knowledge and scholars, in response to one who said 'to the assembly of knowledge', in answer to his saying 'where are you going?' And by his saying 'a bowl of what you want is better than knowledge', not by his saying 'better than Allah' because he intends it as a blessing, and the first has no interpretation except mockery of knowledge. And by the sick person in severe illness saying 'if You wish, cause me to die as a Muslim, and if You wish, as a disbeliever.' And by the afflicted saying 'You took my wealth and took my child and took such and such, so what do You do and what remains?' and by his saying it intentionally, not in response to one who said to him 'Are you not a Muslim?' when he severely beat his slave or child, unless he made a mistake or intended the answer. And by the husband saying 'I have no zeal nor the religion of Islam' when his wife said that to him. And by his saying to a Muslim 'O disbeliever' according to some, even if one of the spouses to the other; and the chosen for fatwa is that he disbelieves if he believes him to be a disbeliever, not if he intended insult. And by his saying 'labayk' in response to one who said 'O disbeliever, O Jew, O Magian.' And by his saying 'I am an atheist' because the atheist is a disbeliever; and if he said 'I did not know it' he is not excused. And by the one apologizing to another saying 'I was a disbeliever and then became Muslim' according to some, and it is said no. And by his saying 'I was a Magian and now I accept Islam.' And by the sinner forgetting repentance, belittling sin, not seeing punishment for sin, and not seeing sins as ugly and acts of obedience as good, and not seeing obedience as good, and not seeing reward for obedience, and not seeing the obligation from Allah... Istibra' is innovation and misguidance, not disbelief. And from Ibrahim ibn Rustam that he said: If he deems permissible intercourse during menstruation interpreting that the prohibition is not for prohibition or if he did not know the prohibition, he does not disbelieve; and if he knew the prohibition and believed the prohibition is for prohibition and then deemed it permissible, he becomes a disbeliever. And from Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi that deeming permissible intercourse during menstruation is disbelief without detail. His statement: (And by the sinner forgetting repentance until his statement: and by his not seeing obedience as good) meaning he disbelieves by seeing the totality... And by his saying 'I disbelieved' when he spoke a word that the people claimed is disbelief but it is not disbelief, so it was said to him 'you disbelieved and your wife is divorced.' And a woman disbelieves if she speaks disbelief with the intention that she become forbidden to her husband while faith is settled in her heart, and her saying 'I become a disbeliever so that I get rid of my husband.' And whoever intends disbelief for an hour or a day is a disbeliever for all his life. And by his wishing for disbelief, that if he were a disbeliever and then became Muslim when he became Muslim as a disbeliever, so he was given something. And by his wishing that injustice, adultery, and murder without right were not prohibited, and every prohibited thing that is not permissible at any time, unlike wine and marrying mahrams. And by his wishing that he were a Christian so he could marry a fat Christian woman he saw. And by placing a Magian cap on his head, according to the correct view, except for necessity to repel heat or cold. And by tying a zunnar around his waist, except if he does it as a trick in war and as a lookout for Muslims. And by the statement of the teacher of Jewish children: 'They are much better than Muslims' because they fulfill the rights of their teachers, and by his saying 'Magianism is better than what I am in', meaning his action. And by his saying 'Christianity is better than Magianism', not by his saying 'Magianism is worse than Christianity.' And by his saying 'Christianity is better than Judaism'; it is proper that he say 'Christianity is worse than Judaism.' And by his saying 'The transaction of disbelief is better than what you do' according to some absolutely; and Abu al-Layth qualified it as intending to beautify disbelief, not to disparage his transaction. And by his going out to the Persian New Year (Nawruz) and agreeing with them in what they do on that day of Nawruz, buying something he did not buy before, to venerate Nawruz not for eating and drinking. And by his gifting on that day to the polytheists even an egg, to venerate that day, not by his accepting an invitation from a Magian who shaved his son's head. And by beautifying the affairs of the disbelievers unanimously; until they said: if he said 'remaining silent during eating from the Magian' or 'not lying with a menstruating woman from them is good', then he is a disbeliever. And by his slaughtering something in front of a person at the time of khil'a or for the one arriving from Hajj or battle, and the slaughtered animal is carrion; and it is said he does not disbelieve. And his saying 'Our present ruler is just'; and it is said no; and upon this difference is the statement of the orators in the titles 'the just greatest sultan, owner of the necks of the nations, sultan of Allah's earth, owner of Allah's lands.' And by his saying 'Do not say to the sultan this' when the sultan sneezed and a man said to him 'May Allah have mercy on you.' And by his giving his child wine to drink, then his relatives came and scattered dirhams and sugar, all disbelieve; likewise if they did not scatter dirhams but said 'blessed.' And they differed regarding if he said 'I love wine and cannot abstain from it.' And he disbelieves by prompting a word of disbelief for him to speak, even if in jest. And by his ordering a woman to apostatize so she becomes separated from her husband, and by issuing a fatwa to that effect, even if the woman does not disbelieve, based on the principle that being pleased with another's disbelief is disbelief; and it is said no. That is why the preposition is not repeated. His statement: (based on the principle that being pleased with another's disbelief is disbelief) as stated in al-Tatarkhaniyya: and in al-Nisab the correct is that he does not disbelieve by being pleased with another's disbelief. And in Ghurar al-Ma'ani: there is no disagreement among our scholars that commanding disbelief is disbelief. And in Sharh al-Siyar: being pleased with another's disbelief is only disbelief if he mocks disbelief and considers it good; but if he loves death or killing on disbelief for someone who is severely harmful by nature so that Allah takes vengeance...
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an extensive enumeration of statements and actions that, according to the Hanafi school, render a Muslim an apostate (murtadd). The text covers a wide range of scenarios, from direct denial of established prohibitions (like wine) to mockery of scholars and religious knowledge, to specific actions such as wearing a Magian cap or participating in non-Islamic festivals. The author often notes differences of opinion (e.g., 'qila' or 'ind ba'dihim') and occasionally provides tarjih (preferred view). The underlying principle is that any explicit rejection of a necessarily known tenet of Islam, or any act that clearly indicates contempt for the religion, constitutes kufr. The text also addresses nuances, such as when a statement is made in jest or out of ignorance, and the importance of intent. The final part discusses the controversial issue of being pleased with another's disbelief (rida bi kufr al-ghayr) and notes that commanding kufr is definitely kufr, but mere approval may not be, according to some authorities. This passage serves as a practical guide for judges and jurists in identifying apostasy.

Key Terms
استخفاف (istikhfaf): Contempt or belittling; actions that show disregard for the sanctity of religion. In Hanafi fiqh, istikhfaf of the sharia is kufr.
استهزاء (istihza'): Mockery; a subset of istikhfaf. The text uses this term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, why is saying 'a bowl of what you want is better than knowledge' considered kufr?
A) Because it compares a bowl to knowledge.
B) Because it has no interpretation other than belittling knowledge.
C) Because it implies knowledge is worthless.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
Mocking religious knowledge, scholars, or sacred texts is kufr because it demonstrates contempt for the religion, regardless of intent.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
advanced
8 min
Acts of Assimilation and Symbols of Disbelief as Apostasy
Enumeration of actions involving assimilation with disbelievers that cause apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify actions that constitute apostasy through external assimilation with disbelievers, such as wearing their symbols or participating in their festivals.

Core Idea
Adopting the outward symbols of disbelief, even without inner conviction, can be kufr if done to venerate them.

The Hanafi jurists also consider certain external actions as signs of apostasy, even if the person claims they do not intend disbelief. These include wearing a Magian cap, tying a zunnar (belt), participating in non-Islamic festivals like Nawruz, and gifting items to polytheists on their religious occasions. The key is whether the act is done to venerate the symbol (تعظيم) or merely for practical reasons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the symbol or act
Look for actions that are specific to other religions, e.g., wearing a Magian cap, tying a zunnar, celebrating Nawruz.
The text lists several specific actions.
2
Determine the intention
If the act is done to venerate the religion or its symbol, it is kufr. If done out of necessity (e.g., for warmth) or trickery (e.g., in war), it may be permissible.
The text explicitly mentions exceptions for necessity and war.
3
Assess if there is approval of disbelief
Gifting an egg to a polytheist on their festival is kufr if done to venerate the day; accepting an invitation to a Magian's celebration may not be kufr if it's just social.
The text distinguishes based on the presence of veneration (تعظيم).
4
Apply the ruling
If the act is done with veneration, the person becomes a disbeliever. If done for worldly reasons, it may be makruh tahrimi but not kufr.
The mufta bihi is the stricter view (kufr) for clear symbols.

بحرام، وقيده بعضهم بما إذا كان يعلم حرمتها لا بقوله الخمر حرام ولكن ليست هذه التي زعمون أنها حرام .، ويكفر من قال إن حرمة الخمر لم تثبت بالقرآن ومن زعم أن الصغائر والكبائر حلال، وباستحلاله الجماع للحائض لا في الاستبراء وقيل لا في الأول وهو الصحيح، ولا باستحلال سؤر كلب أو ريع أرض غصب وباستحلال اللواطة إن علم حرمته من الدين، حلال حين نهى عن تقبيله أجنبية، وبقوله الشريعة كلها تلبيس أو حيل إن قال وبقوله هي . لي في كل الشرائع لا فيما يرجع إلى المعاملات مما تصح فيه الحيل الشرعية وقيل يكفر في الأول مطلقاً ويخاف عليه الكفر إذا شتم عالماً أو فقيهاً من غير سبب، ويكفر بقوله لعالم ذكر الحمار في أست علمك مريداً به علم الدين، وبجلوسه على مكان مرتفع والتشبه بالمذكرين ومع جماعة يسألون منه المسائل ويضحكون منه ثم يضربونه بالمحراق، وكذا يكفر الجميع لاستخفافهم بالشرع، وكذا لو لم يجلس على مكان مرتفع ولكن يستهزئ بالمذكرين ويتمشى والقوم يضحكون، وبإلقاء الفتوى على الأرض حين أتى بها خصمه، وبقوله لا تذهب وإن ذهبت تطلق امرأتك استهزاء بالعلم والعلماء جواباً لمن قال إلى مجلس العلم جواباً لقوله أين تذهب، وبقوله قصعة من تريد خير من العلم لا بقوله خير من الله لإرادته أنها نعمة والأول لا تأويل له سوى الاستخفاف بالعلم، وبقول المريض المشتد مرضه إن شئت توفني مسلماً وإن شئت كافراً، وبقول المبتلي أخذت مالي وأحذت ولدي وأخذت كذا وكذا فماذا تفعل وماذا بقي وبقوله عمداً لا جواباً لمن قال له ألست مسلماً حين ضرب عبده أو ولده ضرباً شديداً إلا إن غلط أو قصد الجواب وبقول الزوج ليس لي حمية ولا دين الإسلام حين قالت له امرأته ذلك، وبقوله لمسلم يا كافر عند البعض ولو أحد الزوجين للآخر والمختار للفتوى أن يكفر إن اعتقده كافراً لا إن أراد شتمه وبقوله لبيك جواباً لمن قال يا كافر يا يهودي يا مجوسي، وبقوله أنا ملحد لأن الملحد كافر ولو قال ما علمته لا يعذر، وبقول المعتذر لغيره كنت كافراً فأسلمت عند بعضهم وقيل لا، وبقوله كنت مجوسياً أسلمت الآن، وبنسيان العاصي التوبة وتحقير الذنب وعدم رؤية العقوبة بالذنب وعدم رؤية المعاصي قبيحة الطاعات ، وبعدم رؤية الطاعة حسناً وبعدم رؤيته الثواب على الطاعة وبعدم رؤيته وجوب من الله الاستبراء بدعة وضلال وليس بكفر وعن إبراهيم بن رستم أنه قال : إن استحل الجماع في الحيض متأولاً أن النهي ليس للتحريم أو لم يعرف النهي لم يكفر، وإن عرف النهي واعتقد أن النهي للتحريم ذلك استحل كان كافراً. وعن شمس الأئمة السرخسي أن استحلال الجماع في الحيض كفر من غير تفصيل . قوله : ( وبنسيان العاصي التوبة إلى قوله وبعدم رؤيته الطاعة حسناء) أي يكفر برؤيته مجموع وبقوله كفرت حين تكلم بكلمة زعم القوم أنها كفر وليست بكفر فقيل له كفرت وطلقت زوجتك، وتكفر المرأة إذا تكلمت بالكفر لقصد أن تحرم على زوجها والإيمان مستقر في قلبها، وقولها أصير كافرة حتى أتخلص من الزوج، ومن قصد الكفر ساعة أو يوماً فهو كافر في جميع العمر، وبتمنيه الكفر أن لو كان كافراً فأسلم حين أسلم كافراً فأعطي شيئاً، وبتمنيه أن لم يحرم الظلم والزنا والقتل بغير حق وكل حرام لا يكون حلالاً في وقت بخلاف الخمر ومناكحة المحارم، وبتمنيه أن لو كان نصرانياً حتى يتزوج نصرانية سمينة رآها، وبوضع قلنسوة المجوسي على رأسه على الصحيح إلا لضرورة دفع الحر أو البرد، وبشد الزنار في وسطه إلا إذا فعل ذلك خديعة في الحرب وطليعة للمسلمين وبقول معلم صبيان اليهود خير من المسلمين بكثير فإنهم يقضون حقوق معلمي صبيانهم وبقوله المجوسية خير مما أنا فيه يعني فعله، وبقوله النصرانية خير من المجوسية لا بقوله المجوسية شر من النصرانية، وبقوله النصرانية خير من اليهودية وينبغي أن يقول النصرانية شر من اليهودية، وبقوله لمعاملة الكفر خير مما أنت تفعل عند بعضهم مطلقاً، وقيده الفقيه أبو الليث بأن يقصد تحسين الكفر لا تقبيح معاملته، وبخروجه إلى نيروز المجوس والموافقة معهم فيما يفعلون في ذلك اليوم النيروز شيئاً لم يكن يشتريه قبل ذلك تعظيماً للنيروز لا للأكل والشرب وبإهدائه ذلك اليوم للمشركين ولو بيضة تعظيماً لذلك اليوم لا بإجابته دعوة مجوسي حلق رأس ولده وبتحسين أمر الكفار اتفاقاً . حتى قالوا: لو قال ترك الكلام عند أكل الطعام من المجوسي أو ترك المضاجعة حالة الحيض منهم حسن فهو كافر. وبذبحه شيئاً في وجه إنسان وقت الخلعة أو للقادم من الحج أو الغزو والمذبوح ميتة وقيل لا يكفر، وقوله لسلطان زماننا عادل وقيل لا وعلى هذا الاختلاف قول الخطباء في ألقاب السلطان العادل الأعظم مالك رقاب الأمم سلطان أرض الله مالك بلاد الله، وبقوله لا تقل للسلطان هذا حين عطس السلطان فقال له رجل يرحمك الله، وبسقي ولده الخمر فجاء أقرباؤه ونثروا الدراهم والسكر كفر الكل، وكذا لو لم ينثروا الدراهم ولكنهم قالوا مبارك، واختلفوا فيما إذا قال أحب الخمر فلا أصبر عنها . ويكفر بتلقين كلمة الكفر ليتكلم بها ولو على وجه اللعب وبأمره امرأة بالارتداد لتبين من زوجها، وبالإفتاء بذلك وإن لم تكفر المرأة بناء على أن الرضا بكفر غيره كفر وقيل لا، ذلك ولذا لم يكرر حرف الجر. قوله : (بناء على الرضا بكفر غيره كفر قال في التتارخانية : وفي النصاب الأصح أنه لا يكفر بالرضا بكفر الغير. وفي غرر المعاني : لا خلاف بين مشايخنا أن الأمر بالكفر كفر. وفي شرح السير : إن الرضا بكفر الغير إنما يكون كفراً إذا كان يستخف الكفر ويستحسنه أما إذا أحب الموت أو القتل على الكفر لمن كان شديداً مؤذياً بطبعه حتى ينتقم الله تعالى
With haram, and some qualified it as when he knows its prohibition, not by his saying 'wine is haram' but it is not this which they claim is haram. And he becomes a disbeliever who says that the prohibition of wine is not established by the Quran, and who claims that minor and major sins are permissible. And by his deeming permissible intercourse with a menstruating woman, not during istibra', and it is said not in the first, and that is correct. And not by deeming permissible the leftover of a dog or the rent of usurped land. And by deeming permissible sodomy if he knows its prohibition from the religion. And by his saying 'the entire sharia is deception or tricks' if he says, and by his saying 'it is for me in all laws, not in what relates to transactions where legal tricks are valid'; and it is said he disbelieves in the first absolutely. And he is feared for disbelief if he insults a scholar or jurist without cause. And he disbelieves by his saying to a scholar 'mention the donkey in the anus of your knowledge' intending thereby religious knowledge. And by his sitting in an elevated place and imitating the preachers, and with a group asking him questions and laughing at him, then they strike him with a firebrand; likewise all disbelieve for their mockery of the law. Likewise if he did not sit in an elevated place but mocks the preachers and walks while the people laugh. And by throwing the fatwa on the ground when his opponent brought it. And by his saying 'don't go, and if you go your wife is divorced' as mockery of knowledge and scholars, in response to one who said 'to the assembly of knowledge', in answer to his saying 'where are you going?' And by his saying 'a bowl of what you want is better than knowledge', not by his saying 'better than Allah' because he intends it as a blessing, and the first has no interpretation except mockery of knowledge. And by the sick person in severe illness saying 'if You wish, cause me to die as a Muslim, and if You wish, as a disbeliever.' And by the afflicted saying 'You took my wealth and took my child and took such and such, so what do You do and what remains?' and by his saying it intentionally, not in response to one who said to him 'Are you not a Muslim?' when he severely beat his slave or child, unless he made a mistake or intended the answer. And by the husband saying 'I have no zeal nor the religion of Islam' when his wife said that to him. And by his saying to a Muslim 'O disbeliever' according to some, even if one of the spouses to the other; and the chosen for fatwa is that he disbelieves if he believes him to be a disbeliever, not if he intended insult. And by his saying 'labayk' in response to one who said 'O disbeliever, O Jew, O Magian.' And by his saying 'I am an atheist' because the atheist is a disbeliever; and if he said 'I did not know it' he is not excused. And by the one apologizing to another saying 'I was a disbeliever and then became Muslim' according to some, and it is said no. And by his saying 'I was a Magian and now I accept Islam.' And by the sinner forgetting repentance, belittling sin, not seeing punishment for sin, and not seeing sins as ugly and acts of obedience as good, and not seeing obedience as good, and not seeing reward for obedience, and not seeing the obligation from Allah... Istibra' is innovation and misguidance, not disbelief. And from Ibrahim ibn Rustam that he said: If he deems permissible intercourse during menstruation interpreting that the prohibition is not for prohibition or if he did not know the prohibition, he does not disbelieve; and if he knew the prohibition and believed the prohibition is for prohibition and then deemed it permissible, he becomes a disbeliever. And from Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi that deeming permissible intercourse during menstruation is disbelief without detail. His statement: (And by the sinner forgetting repentance until his statement: and by his not seeing obedience as good) meaning he disbelieves by seeing the totality... And by his saying 'I disbelieved' when he spoke a word that the people claimed is disbelief but it is not disbelief, so it was said to him 'you disbelieved and your wife is divorced.' And a woman disbelieves if she speaks disbelief with the intention that she become forbidden to her husband while faith is settled in her heart, and her saying 'I become a disbeliever so that I get rid of my husband.' And whoever intends disbelief for an hour or a day is a disbeliever for all his life. And by his wishing for disbelief, that if he were a disbeliever and then became Muslim when he became Muslim as a disbeliever, so he was given something. And by his wishing that injustice, adultery, and murder without right were not prohibited, and every prohibited thing that is not permissible at any time, unlike wine and marrying mahrams. And by his wishing that he were a Christian so he could marry a fat Christian woman he saw. And by placing a Magian cap on his head, according to the correct view, except for necessity to repel heat or cold. And by tying a zunnar around his waist, except if he does it as a trick in war and as a lookout for Muslims. And by the statement of the teacher of Jewish children: 'They are much better than Muslims' because they fulfill the rights of their teachers, and by his saying 'Magianism is better than what I am in', meaning his action. And by his saying 'Christianity is better than Magianism', not by his saying 'Magianism is worse than Christianity.' And by his saying 'Christianity is better than Judaism'; it is proper that he say 'Christianity is worse than Judaism.' And by his saying 'The transaction of disbelief is better than what you do' according to some absolutely; and Abu al-Layth qualified it as intending to beautify disbelief, not to disparage his transaction. And by his going out to the Persian New Year (Nawruz) and agreeing with them in what they do on that day of Nawruz, buying something he did not buy before, to venerate Nawruz not for eating and drinking. And by his gifting on that day to the polytheists even an egg, to venerate that day, not by his accepting an invitation from a Magian who shaved his son's head. And by beautifying the affairs of the disbelievers unanimously; until they said: if he said 'remaining silent during eating from the Magian' or 'not lying with a menstruating woman from them is good', then he is a disbeliever. And by his slaughtering something in front of a person at the time of khil'a or for the one arriving from Hajj or battle, and the slaughtered animal is carrion; and it is said he does not disbelieve. And his saying 'Our present ruler is just'; and it is said no; and upon this difference is the statement of the orators in the titles 'the just greatest sultan, owner of the necks of the nations, sultan of Allah's earth, owner of Allah's lands.' And by his saying 'Do not say to the sultan this' when the sultan sneezed and a man said to him 'May Allah have mercy on you.' And by his giving his child wine to drink, then his relatives came and scattered dirhams and sugar, all disbelieve; likewise if they did not scatter dirhams but said 'blessed.' And they differed regarding if he said 'I love wine and cannot abstain from it.' And he disbelieves by prompting a word of disbelief for him to speak, even if in jest. And by his ordering a woman to apostatize so she becomes separated from her husband, and by issuing a fatwa to that effect, even if the woman does not disbelieve, based on the principle that being pleased with another's disbelief is disbelief; and it is said no. That is why the preposition is not repeated. His statement: (based on the principle that being pleased with another's disbelief is disbelief) as stated in al-Tatarkhaniyya: and in al-Nisab the correct is that he does not disbelieve by being pleased with another's disbelief. And in Ghurar al-Ma'ani: there is no disagreement among our scholars that commanding disbelief is disbelief. And in Sharh al-Siyar: being pleased with another's disbelief is only disbelief if he mocks disbelief and considers it good; but if he loves death or killing on disbelief for someone who is severely harmful by nature so that Allah takes vengeance...
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an extensive enumeration of statements and actions that, according to the Hanafi school, render a Muslim an apostate (murtadd). The text covers a wide range of scenarios, from direct denial of established prohibitions (like wine) to mockery of scholars and religious knowledge, to specific actions such as wearing a Magian cap or participating in non-Islamic festivals. The author often notes differences of opinion (e.g., 'qila' or 'ind ba'dihim') and occasionally provides tarjih (preferred view). The underlying principle is that any explicit rejection of a necessarily known tenet of Islam, or any act that clearly indicates contempt for the religion, constitutes kufr. The text also addresses nuances, such as when a statement is made in jest or out of ignorance, and the importance of intent. The final part discusses the controversial issue of being pleased with another's disbelief (rida bi kufr al-ghayr) and notes that commanding kufr is definitely kufr, but mere approval may not be, according to some authorities. This passage serves as a practical guide for judges and jurists in identifying apostasy.

Key Terms
تعظيم (ta'zim): Veneration; showing respect or honoring something. When applied to symbols of kufr, it causes apostasy.
نيروز (nayruz / nawruz): Persian New Year, a festival of the Magians. Participating with veneration is kufr.
زي النصارى (ziy al-nasara): Clothing of the Christians; wearing distinctive religious attire without necessity is kufr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, why is tying a zunnar (belt) not kufr if done as a trick in war?
A) Because it is necessary for military strategy.
B) Because war permits any deception.
C) Because the act is not done with veneration.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
Adopting outward symbols of disbelief or participating in their religious festivals with veneration is kufr, even if the heart is not convinced.

Caution in Takfir: General Principles
Commentator's introduction to caution in takfir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that takfir is avoided if any doubt or good interpretation exists, and identify the categories of utterances (joking, mistake, coercion, intention, ignorance) and their rulings.

Core Idea
Takfir is a grave matter; a Muslim is never declared a disbeliever as long as any doubt or favourable interpretation remains.

This passage sets the foundational principle for the entire chapter on apostates. The commentator warns against hasty takfir, emphasising that established Islam cannot be overturned by doubt. You will learn the key maxims that guide a mufti when faced with potentially incriminating statements from a Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overriding principle
Identify the statement 'established Islam is not removed by doubt' and recognise its implications: any uncertainty must weigh against takfir.
This principle is derived from the general Hanafi legal maxim 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk'.
2
Classify the types of utterances
From the quoted sources, list the categories: joking/playing, mistake, coercion, intentional, ignorant. Note the ruling for each as mentioned in the text.
The categories are mutually exclusive; the ruling depends on mental state and awareness.
3
Apply the mufti's rule of caution
When multiple aspects exist (some requiring takfir, one preventing it), the mufti must incline to the aspect preventing takfir. Understand that even a weak report that the person is not a disbeliever suffices.
This is from al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya; the exception is when the person explicitly intends the meaning of kufr.
4
Recognise the effect of interpretation
If the statement can be interpreted in a good way, takfir is not pronounced. This is the settled position (mufta bihi).
The commentator personally commits never to issue a fatwa of takfir on such expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير باب أحكام المرتدين
في
ردة يحكم بها به وما يشك أنه ردة لا يحكم بها إذ الإسلام الثابت لا يزول بشك مع أن الإسلام يعلو، وينبغي للعالم إذا رفع إليه هذا أن لا يبادر بتكفير أهل الإسلام مع أنه يقضي بصحة إسلام المكره . أقول : قدمت هذه لتصير ميزاناً فيما نقلته في هذا الفصل من المسائل فإنه قد ذكر في بعضها أنه كفر مع أنه لا يكفر على قياس هذه المقدمة فليتأمل اهـ. وفي الفتاوى الصغرى : الكفر شيء عظيم فلا أجعل المؤمن كافراً متى وجدت رواية أنه لا يكفر اهـ. وقال قبله وفي الجامع الأصغر، إذا أطلق الرجل كلمة الكفر عمداً لكنه لم يعتقد الكفر قال بعض أصحابنا : لا يكفر لأن الكفر يتعلق بالضمير ولم يعقد الضمير على الكفر. وقال بعضهم : يكفر وهو الصحيح عندي لأنه استخف بدينه اهـ. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها: إذا كان المسألة وجوه توجب التكفير ووجه واحد يمنع التكفير فعلى المفتي أن يميل إلى الوجه الذي يمنع التكفير تحسيناً للظن بالمسلم زاد في البزازية إلا إذا صرح بإرادة موجب الكفر فلا ينفعه التأويل حينئذ . وفي التتارخانية : لا يكفر بالمحتمل لأن الكفر نهاية في العقوبة فيستدعي نهاية في الجناية ومع الاحتمال لا نهاية .اهـ. والحاصل أن من تكلم بكلمة الكفر هازلاً أو لاعباً كفر عند الكل ولا اعتبار باعتقاده كما صرح به قاضيخان في فتاواه، ومن تكلم بها مخطئاً أو مكرهاً لا يكفر عند الكل، ومن تكلم بها عالماً عامداً كفر عند الكل، ومن تكلم بها اختياراً جاهلاً بأنها كفر ففيه اختلاف، والذي تحرر أنه لا يفتى بتكفير مسلم أمكن حمل كلامه على محمل حسن أو كان في كفره اختلاف ولو رواية ضعيفة، فعلى هذا فأكثر ألفاظ التكفير المذكورة لا يفتى بالتكفير بها ولقد ألزمت نفسي أن لا أفتي بشيء منها. وأما مسألة تكفير أهل البدع المذكورة في الفتاوى فقد تركتها عمداً لأن محلها أصول الدين وقد أوضحها المحقق في المسايرة.
The Book of Siyar, Chapter on Rulings of Apostates. Regarding apostasy that is ruled upon, and what is doubted to be apostasy is not ruled upon, because established Islam is not removed by doubt, while Islam prevails. It is incumbent upon the scholar, when this is brought to him, not to hasten to declare the people of Islam as disbelievers, even though he rules for the validity of the Islam of the coerced. I say: I have presented this to serve as a criterion for what I have transmitted in this chapter of issues, for it has been mentioned in some of them that it is kufr while it is not kufr according to the measure of this premise, so let it be pondered. In al-Fatawa al-Sughra: Kufr is a great matter, so I do not consider a believer a disbeliever as long as I find a report that he is not a disbeliever. And before it, in al-Jami' al-Asghar: If a man utters a word of kufr intentionally but does not believe in kufr, some of our companions said: He is not a disbeliever because kufr pertains to the inner conscience and he did not intend kufr in his heart. Others said: He is a disbeliever, and that is correct in my view because he has belittled his religion. In al-Khulasa and others: If in a case there are aspects that necessitate takfir and one aspect that prevents takfir, the mufti should incline to the aspect that prevents takfir, to think well of the Muslim. Added in al-Bazzaziyya: Unless he explicitly declares intent for the implication of kufr, then interpretation does not benefit him. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: He is not declared a disbeliever by a probable matter because kufr is extreme in punishment, so it requires extremity in the crime, and with probability there is no extremity. The summary: Whoever utters a word of kufr jokingly or playfully is a disbeliever according to all, and his belief is not considered, as Qadikhan stated in his Fatawa. Whoever utters it mistakenly or under coercion is not a disbeliever according to all. Whoever utters it knowingly and intentionally is a disbeliever according to all. Whoever utters it willingly but ignorantly of it being kufr, there is disagreement. What is established is that a Muslim is not given a fatwa of takfir if his words can be carried to a good interpretation, or if there is disagreement about his kufr, even with a weak report. Hence, most of the mentioned expressions of takfir are not given fatwa of takfir thereby. I have obligated myself not to give a fatwa on any of them. As for the issue of takfir of the people of innovation mentioned in the Fatawa, I have deliberately left it because its place is in usul al-din, and the investigator has clarified it in al-Musayara.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is the commentator's introduction to the chapter on apostates. He establishes a fundamental principle: Islam, once established, cannot be overturned by doubt. He warns scholars not to be hasty in declaring Muslims as apostates. He then quotes various fatwa collections emphasizing caution. The overall message is that takfir (excommunication) is a grave matter and must be avoided whenever possible. He summarizes rules for different scenarios: joking or playing results in kufr; mistake or coercion does not; intentional action does; ignorance is disputed. The settled position is that if any good interpretation or even a weak report prevents takfir, the mufti should not declare takfir. The commentator personally commits to never issue a fatwa of takfir based on such expressions.

Key Terms
ردة (riddah): Apostasy; the act of a Muslim abandoning Islam.
تكفير (takfir): The act of declaring someone to be a disbeliever (kafir).
كفر (kufr): Disbelief; the state of being outside Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what should a mufti do if there are multiple aspects in a case, some requiring takfir and one preventing it?
A) He must rule with takfir to be safe.
B) He should incline to the aspect preventing takfir to think well of the Muslim.
C) He must refer to the ruler.
D) He should declare the person an apostate and then allow repentance.

Key Takeaway
Established Islam is not removed by doubt; a mufti must always seek a way to avoid takfir, even if a weak report exists that the person is not a disbeliever.

Procedure for Apostates: Presenting Islam, Clarifying Doubts, and Imprisonment
Commentary explaining the three-step procedure for an apostate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for dealing with an apostate, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over presenting Islam, and apply the rules for repeated apostasy.

Core Idea
An apostate is given three days to repent; presenting Islam is recommended, not obligatory, and doubts are clarified.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq lays out the three-step procedure for handling an apostate: presenting Islam, clarifying any doubts, and imprisonment for three days. The commentator explores whether presenting Islam is obligatory or recommended, citing a difference between the apparent madhhab and other narrations. Understanding this procedure is critical for correctly applying the hudud rulings on apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three steps
Locate the three elements mentioned in the matn: presenting Islam (ard al-Islam), clarifying doubts (kashf al-shubhah), and imprisonment (habs) for three days. Note the purpose of each.
The matn is quoted at the beginning of the passage.
2
Analyse the ruling on presenting Islam
Examine the statement 'ظاهر المذهب استحبابه فقط' (the apparent madhhab is that it is only recommended). Understand the proof: because the da'wah has already reached the apostate. Contrast this with the view that it is wajib and with the exception when the apostate requests respite.
The commentator cites al-Mabsut for the wajib view if respite is requested.
3
Understand the clarification of doubts
Recognise that clarifying doubts is the benefit of presenting Islam. The apostate may have a shubhah that caused his apostasy; the imam should address it.
This is tied to the presentation itself.
4
Examine the imprisonment period
The three days are set to give the apostate a chance to offer excuses, based on a narration from Umar. Note the disagreement: one view grants respite even without request; the apparent narration requires a request. Understand the implication for immediate execution vs. deferral.
The text says 'ظاهر الرواية أنه لا يمهل بدون استمهال'.
5
Apply the rules for repeated apostasy
Read the section on second and third apostasy: on second repentance, beating and release; on third, beating, imprisonment until sincere repentance. Note that the general rule is acceptance of repentance except for sabb (insulting the Prophet), which follows next.
This shows the graduated response in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (يعرض الإسلام على (المرتد أي يعرضه الإمام والقاضي وهو مروي عن عمر الله عنه لأن رجاء العود إلى الإسلام ثابت لاحتمال أن الردة كانت باعتراض شبهة لم يبين صفته، وظاهر المذهب استحبابه فقط ولا يجب لأن الدعوة قد بلغته وعرض الإسلام هو الدعوة إليه ودعوة من بلغته الدعوى غير واجبة ولم يذكر تكرار العرض عليه. وفي الخانية : يعرض عليه الإسلام في كل يوم من أيام التأجيل . قوله : ( وتكشف شبهته) بيان لفائدة العرض أي فإن كان له شبهة أبداها كشفت عنه لأنه عساه اعترضت له شبهة فتزاح عنه . قوله : ( ويحبس ثلاثة أيام فإن أسلم وإلا قتل لأنها مدة ضربت لإبداء الأعذار وهو مروي عن عمر رضي الله عنه أطلقه فأفاد أنه يمهل وإن لم يطلبه وهو رواية، وظاهر الرواية أنه لا يمهل بدون استمهال بل يقتل من ساعته كما في الجامع الصغير إلا إذا كان الإمام يرجو رضي قوله : (لم يبين صفته أي صفة العرض. وذكر في النهر أن قوله يعرض» ظاهر في وجوبه كما في إسلامه كما في البدائع. وإذا استمهل فظاهر المبسوط الوجوب فإنه قال : إذا طلب التأجيل كان على الإمام أن يمهله وعن الإمام الاستحباب مطلقاً. وأفاد بإطلاقه أنه يفعل به ذلك إذا ارتد ثانياً إلا أنه إذا تاب ضربه الإمام وخلى سبيله، وإن ارتد ثالثاً ثم تاب ضربه الإمام ضرباً وجيعاً وحبسه حتى تظهر عليه التوبة ويرى أنه مسلم مخلص ثم خلى سبيله فإن عاد فعل به أنه هكذا؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وأفاد بإطلاقه أنه لا فرق بين ردة وردة من إذا أسلم
His saying: 'Islam is presented to the apostate' meaning the imam and judge present it, and it is narrated from Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, because hope of return to Islam is established due to the possibility that the apostasy was due to a doubt whose nature is not specified. The apparent madhhab is that it is only recommended (mustahabb) and not obligatory because the da'wah has already reached him, and presenting Islam is the da'wah, and calling one whom the da'wah has reached is not obligatory. And he did not mention repetition of the presentation. In al-Khaniyya: Islam is presented to him every day of the deferral period. His saying: 'And his doubt is clarified' is an explanation of the benefit of the presentation, i.e., if he has a doubt, he expresses it, and it is clarified for him because perhaps a doubt occurred to him and is removed. His saying: 'And he is imprisoned for three days; if he becomes Muslim, otherwise he is killed' because that period is set for presenting excuses, and it is narrated from Umar, may Allah be pleased with him. He left it unrestricted, thus indicating that he is given respite even if he does not request it, and that is one narration. The apparent narration is that he is not given respite without a request, but is killed immediately, as in al-Jami' al-Saghir, unless the imam hopes... His saying: 'He did not specify its nature' meaning the nature of the presentation. And it is mentioned in al-Nahr that his saying 'presents' apparently indicates obligation, as in... his (the apostate's) Islam, as in al-Bada'i'. If he requests a respite, the apparent in al-Mabsut is obligation, for he said: If he requests deferral, the imam must give him respite. From the Imam (Abu Hanifa) it is reported that it is recommended absolutely. And he indicated by his unrestricted statement that this is done to him if he apostatizes a second time, except that if he repents, the imam beats him and releases him. If he apostatizes a third time and then repents, the imam beats him severely and imprisons him until his repentance becomes apparent and it is seen that he is a sincere Muslim, then releases him. If he returns, it is done to him likewise. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And he indicated by his unrestricted statement that there is no difference between one apostasy and another as long as he becomes Muslim [before the exception].
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the procedure for an apostate. The matn states three steps: presenting Islam, clarifying doubts, and imprisonment for three days. The commentator explains that the presentation is done by the imam or judge, and it is recommended (mustahabb) not obligatory according to the apparent madhhab, because the apostate already received the call to Islam. Some authorities hold it as wajib, but the relied-upon view is mustahabb. The clarification of doubts is to address any confusion that may have led to apostasy. The three-day imprisonment is set as a period for the apostate to offer excuses or repent. There is a difference of narration: one view grants respite even without request; the stronger view requires a request. The commentary also covers repeated apostasy: on the second apostasy, if he repents, he is beaten and released; on the third, he is beaten and imprisoned until his repentance is clear. The general rule is that an apostate who returns to Islam is accepted, with an exception for the case of insulting the Prophet (sabb), discussed next.

Key Terms
عرض الإسلام (ard al-Islam): Presenting the testimony of faith to the apostate and inviting him to return to Islam.
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or confusion that may have led the person to apostasy.
حبس (habs): Imprisonment for three days to give the apostate a chance to repent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent madhhab, is presenting Islam to the apostate obligatory or recommended?
A) Obligatory (wajib).
B) Recommended (mustahabb).
C) Forbidden.
D) It depends on the imam's discretion.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi procedure for apostates balances mercy and deterrence: presenting Islam (mustahabb), clarifying doubts, and imprisoning three days before execution, with graduated responses for repeated apostasy.

Apostasy by Insulting the Prophet: Dispute over Ruling and Repentance
Detailed discussion of the exception: apostasy by sabb al-rasul and whether repentance is accepted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on whether repentance is accepted from one who insults the Prophet, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Insulting the Prophet is apostasy, but accepting repentance to avoid execution is disputed among Hanafis.

This passage delves into a contentious exception within the law of apostasy: the case of sabb al-rasul (insulting the Prophet). While general apostasy allows for repentance to avert execution, many scholars argue that the insult of the Prophet is a special hadd crime that cannot be waived by repentance. We will trace the intra-Hanafi debate and the commentator's preferred position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
List the two Hanafi views: (1) repentance accepted (general rule applies), (2) repentance not accepted (hadd punishment executed regardless).
The commentator sides with the second view.
2
Examine the sources cited
Note the authorities: Fath al-Qadir, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Nutaf, al-Shifa', al-Jawhara, al-Subki. Consider which early Hanafi figures support each position.
The text shows attribution debates.
3
Analyze the commentator's tarjih
Identify why the commentator prefers non-acceptance: to protect the Prophet's honor, and because it is the position of al-Jawhara and al-Subki.
He states it should be relied upon in fatwa and judiciary.
4
Distinguish inter-madhhab from intra-madhhab
Note that the Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools unanimously hold non-acceptance, while Hanafis are split.
This makes it a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويستثنى منه مسائل : الأولى الردة بسبه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال في فتح القدير : كل من أبغض رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بقلبه كان مرتداً فالساب بطريق أولى ثم يقتل حداً عندنا فلا تقبل توبته في إسقاطه القتل. قالوا : الفتح، فقوله «لم يبين صفته ممنوع نعم ظاهر المذهب أنه مندوب فقط . قوله : (قال في فتح القدير كل من أبغض رسول الله تعالى الخ) قال تلميذ المؤلف في منح الغفار بعد نقله ذلك وجعله إياه متناً ما نصه : وبمثله صرح الإمام البزازي وبهذا جزم شيخنا في فوائده لكن سمعت من مولانا شيخ الإسلام أمين الدين بن عبد العالم مفتي الحنفية بالديار المصرية أن صاحب الفتح تبع البزازي في ذلك وأن البزازي تبع صاحب الصارم المسلول فإنه عزا في البزازية ما نقله من ذلك إليه ولم يعزه إلى أحد علماء الحنفية اهـ. وقد نقل ابن أفلاطون زاده في كتابه المسمى بمعين الحكام أنها ردة حيث قال من معزياً إلى شرح الطحاوي ما صورته من سب النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أو بغضه كان ذلك منه ردة وحكمه حكم المرتدين .اهـ. وفي النتف : من سب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فإنه مرتد وحكمه حكم المرتد ويفعل به ما يفعل بالمرتد .اهـ. فقوله ويفعل به ما يفعل بالمرتد ظاهر في قبول توبته كما لا يخفى . وممن نقل أنها ردة عن أبي حنيفة القاضي عياض في كتابه المسمى بالشفاء ونص عبارته : قال أبو بكر بن المنذري رحمه الله تعالى : أجمع عوام أهل العلم على أن من سب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقتل. وممن قال ذلك مالك أنس والليث وأحمد وإسحاق وهو مذهب الشافعي رحمه الله. قال القاضي أبو الفضل: وهو مقتضى قول أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله تعالى عنه . ولا تقبل توبته عند هؤلاء وبمثله قال أبو حنيفة وأصحابه والثوري وأهل الكوفة والأوزاعي في المسلم لكنهم قالوا: هي ردة. وروى مثله الوليد بن مسلم عن مالك رحمه الله وحكى الطبري مثله عن أبي حنيفة وأصحابه فيمن ينقصه صلى الله عليه وسلم أو برئ منه أو كذبه اهـ إلى هنا كلام صاحب المنح. لكن قال بعدما يأتي عن الجوهرة في ساب الشيخين أقول : يقوى القول بعدم قبول توبة من سب صاحب الشرع الشريف وهو الذي ينبغي أن يعول عليه في الإفتاء والقضاء رعاية لحضرة صاحب الرسالة المخصوص بكمال الفضل والبسالة .اهـ. وفيه كلام تعرفه وقد حررت المسألة في تنقيح الحامدية فراجعها، ثم جمعت في ذلك كتاباً سميته تنبيه الولاة والحكام على أحكام شاتم خير الأنام أو أحد أصحابه الكرام عليه وعليهم الصلاة والسلام، وبينت فيه أن قول الشفاء «لكنهم قالوا هي ردة الخ صريح في قبول توبته لأنه استدراك على قوله قبله يقتل ولا تقبل توبته عند هؤلاء فعلم أن قوله وبمثله قال أبو حنيفة» أي قال إنه يقتل لكن قالوا إنه ردة فحاصله أنه يقتل إن لم يتب كما هو حكم الردة وإلا لم يكن للاستدراك المذكور فائدة وممن صرح بقبول توبته عندنا الإمام السبكي في السيف المسلول وقال : إنه
An exception is made for cases: First, apostasy by insulting him (the Prophet), may Allah bless him and grant him peace. He said in Fath al-Qadir: Whoever hates the Messenger of Allah in his heart is an apostate, and the one who insults is even more so. Then he is killed as a hadd punishment according to us, and his repentance is not accepted in terms of dropping the killing. They said: In Fath, his saying 'he did not specify its nature' is prevented. Yes, the apparent madhhab is that it is only recommended. His saying: 'He said in Fath al-Qadir: Whoever hates the Messenger of Allah...' The student of the author said in Manh al-Ghaffar after transmitting that and making it as a matn, the text: 'Similarly, Imam al-Bazzazi explicitly stated, and our shaykh affirmed it in his Fawa'id. But I heard from our master, Shaykh al-Islam Amin al-Din ibn 'Abd al-'Alam, mufti of the Hanafis in Egypt, that the author of Fath followed al-Bazzazi in that, and al-Bazzazi followed the author of al-Sarim al-Maslul, for he attributed in al-Bazzaziyya what he transmitted to him, and did not attribute it to any Hanafi scholar.' And Ibn Aflatun Zada transmitted in his book Mu'in al-Hukkam that it is apostasy, saying, attributing to Sharh al-Tahawi: 'Whoever insults the Prophet or hates him, that is apostasy from him, and his ruling is the ruling of apostates.' In al-Nutaf: 'Whoever insults the Messenger of Allah is an apostate and his ruling is the ruling of an apostate, and what is done to an apostate is done to him.' So his saying 'and what is done to an apostate is done to him' apparently indicates acceptance of his repentance, as is not hidden. Among those who transmitted it as apostasy from Abu Hanifa is al-Qadi 'Iyad in his book al-Shifa', and the text of his statement: Abu Bakr ibn al-Mundhir said: The general scholars have agreed that whoever insults the Prophet is killed. Among those who said that are Malik, al-Layth, Ahmad, and Ishaq, and it is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i. Al-Qadi Abu al-Fadl said: It follows from the statement of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. And their repentance is not accepted according to these, and similarly Abu Hanifa and his companions, al-Thawri, the people of Kufa, and al-Awza'i said regarding the Muslim, but they said it is apostasy. And al-Walid ibn Muslim narrated similarly from Malik, and al-Tabari narrated similarly from Abu Hanifa and his companions regarding one who diminishes him or disowns him or denies him. Thus far the words of the author of al-Manh. But he said after what will come from al-Jawhara regarding the one who insults the two shaykhs: I say: The opinion that the repentance of one who insults the master of the noble Shari'ah is not accepted is strong, and it is what should be relied upon in fatwa and judiciary, out of respect for the master of the message, who is distinguished by complete virtue and bravery. In there is discussion you know, and I have investigated the issue in Tanqih al-Hamidiyya, so refer to it. Then I compiled a book on it named Tanbih al-Wulah wa al-Hukkam 'ala Ahkam Shatim Khair al-Anam aw Ahad Ashabihi al-Kiram. And I clarified in it that the statement of al-Shifa' 'but they said it is apostasy' is explicit in accepting his repentance, because it is an exception to his preceding statement 'he is killed and his repentance is not accepted according to these'. So it is known that his statement 'and similarly Abu Hanifa said' means he said he is killed but they said it is apostasy. So the gist is that he is killed if he does not repent, as is the ruling of apostasy; otherwise the aforementioned exception would have no benefit. Among those who explicitly accepted his repentance according to us is Imam al-Subki in al-Saif al-Maslul, and he said: ...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is an extensive discussion on the exception to the general rule that an apostate's repentance is accepted. The exception is for one who insults the Prophet (sabb al-rasul). The commentator examines conflicting views. Some Hanafi authorities like Fath al-Qadir hold that such a person is killed as a hadd punishment and his repentance does not spare him from execution. Others, including some Hanafi texts like al-Nutaf and the view of al-Subki, hold that it is still apostasy and repentance is accepted as per the general rule. The commentator sides with the view that repentance is not accepted, to protect the honor of the Prophet. He also discusses the attribution of views to Abu Hanifa and other early scholars. The dispute is both inter-madhhab (with Shafi'i, Maliki, etc. who say repentance not accepted) and intra-Hanafi (some Hanafis say it is apostasy with repentance accepted, others say no). The passage concludes with the commentator's own work on the subject and his preference for non-acceptance of repentance.

Key Terms
سب (sabb): Insulting or reviling, specifically against the Prophet.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law; here, execution for insulting the Prophet.
توبة (tawbah): Repentance from apostasy; in general apostasy, it saves from execution, but disputed in case of sabb.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator's preferred view, what is the ruling on the repentance of someone who insults the Prophet?
A) His repentance is accepted and he is not killed.
B) His repentance is not accepted and he is killed regardless.
C) He is not considered an apostate.
D) He is only punished with imprisonment.

Key Takeaway
Insulting the Prophet is apostasy, but the relied-upon Hanafi view is that repentance does not avert the death penalty, upholding the inviolability of the Prophet.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

15 min
The Hadd of Slandering the Prophet: Does Repentance Dropthe Punishment?
Dispute over acceptance of repentance for slandering the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that repentance does not drop the hadd for slandering the Prophet, and evaluate the reasoning behind the opposing view.

Core Idea
Slandering the Prophet incurs a hadd that repentance cannot erase—because a human right is attached.

This passage deals with a severe crime: apostasy through slander of the Prophet (saw). The central question is whether sincere repentance cancels the fixed punishment of execution. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement, but the relied-upon position is that repentance does not nullify the hadd. This lesson will unpack the arguments and the legal reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the crime and its classification
Slandering the Prophet constitutes apostasy (ridda) according to Abu Hanifa and his school. Determine what makes this crime distinct from other forms of apostasy.
The crime is both ridda and a hadd violation.
2
State the core dispute
Two positions exist within Hanafi fiqh: one holds that repentance is accepted and the killing is dropped, the other holds that repentance does not drop the hadd. Identify the proponents of each view.
The dispute centers on whether a human right (haqq al-‘abd) is involved.
3
Analyze the evidence for each side
The view that repentance is not accepted analogizes to the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of adultery), which is a right of the servant and not dropped by repentance. The opposing view argues that since it is ridda, the general rule of accepting repentance for apostasy applies.
The passage from al-Shifa provides a key istidrak (qualification).
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The author of Bahr al-Raiq, after reviewing the sources, adopts the view that repentance does not drop the killing, but notes the difference of opinion. Identify the tarjih mechanism: reliance on Fath al-Qadir and the principle of honoring the Prophet.
The mufta bihi is execution even after repentance.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Consider how this ruling applies if the slanderer repents voluntarily, or if he slanders while drunk. Also distinguish between slander of the Prophet and slander of Allah.
The ruling is specific to the Prophet; slander of Allah accepts repentance.

الشرع الشريف وهو الذي ينبغي أن يعول عليه في الإفتاء والقضاء رعاية لحضرة صاحب الرسالة المخصوص بكمال الفضل والبسالة .اهـ. وفيه كلام تعرفه وقد حررت المسألة في تنقيح الحامدية فراجعها، ثم جمعت في ذلك
