قبله يقتل ولا تقبل توبته عند هؤلاء فعلم أن قوله وبمثله قال أبو حنيفة» أي قال إنه يقتل لكن قالوا إنه ردة فحاصله أنه يقتل إن لم يتب كما هو حكم الردة وإلا لم يكن للاستدراك المذكور فائدة وممن صرح بقبول توبته عندنا الإمام السبكي في السيف المسلول وقال : إنه أن هذا مذهب أهل الكوفة ومالك، ونقل عن أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه . ولا فرق بين يجيء تائباً . من نفسه أو شهد عليه بذلك بخلاف غيره من المكفرات فإن الإنكار فيها توبة فلا تعمل الشهادة معه حتى قالوا يقتل وإن سب سكران ولا يعفى عنه ولا بد من تقييده بما إذا كان سكره بسبب محظور باشره مختاراً بلا إكراه وإلا فهو كالمجنون. قال الخطابي : لا أعلم أحداً خالف في وجوب قتله وأما مثله في حقه تعالى فتقبل توبته في إسقاط قتله اهـ. وعلله البزازي بأنه حق تعلق به حق العبد فلا يسقط بالتوبة كسائر حقوق الآدميين وكحد القذف لا يزول بالتوبة، وصرح بأن سب واحد من الأنبياء كذلك. وقوله في فتح القدير في إسقاط القتل يفيد أن توبته مقبولة عند الله تعالى وهو مصرح به.
And he indicated by his absolute statement that there is no difference between one apostasy and another for one who becomes Muslim, but exceptions are made for certain issues: First: Apostasy by slandering him (the Prophet) may Allah bless him and grant him peace. He said in Fath al-Qadir: Whoever hates the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) in his heart becomes an apostate, so the slanderer is more obviously so, then he is killed as a fixed punishment (hadd) according to us, and his repentance is not accepted to drop the killing. They said: Fath, so his statement 'he did not specify its description' is denied; indeed the apparent madhhab is that it is only recommended. His statement (he said in Fath al-Qadir: whoever hates Allah's Messenger etc.): The author's student said in Manh al-Ghaffar after quoting that and making it a text: The Imam al-Bazzazi explicitly stated similarly, and our teacher affirmed it in his Fa'id, but I heard from our master Shaykh al-Islam Amin al-Din ibn Abd al-Alam, the Hanafi mufti in the Egyptian lands, that the author of Fath followed al-Bazzazi in that, and that al-Bazzazi followed the author of al-Sarim al-Maslul, for he attributed in al-Bazzaziyya what he quoted from that to him and did not attribute it to any Hanafi scholar. Ibn Aflatun Zada in his book Mu'in al-Hukkam transmitted that it is apostasy, saying, quoting from Sharh al-Tahawi: Whoever slanders the Prophet (upon him be peace) or hates him, that is apostasy from him and his ruling is the ruling of apostates. And in al-Nutaf: Whoever slanders the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) is an apostate and his ruling is the ruling of the apostate, and one does to him what is done to the apostate. So his statement 'and one does to him what is done to the apostate' is apparent in accepting his repentance, as is not hidden. And among those who transmitted that it is apostasy from Abu Hanifa is Qadi Iyad in his book al-Shifa, and the text of his statement: Abu Bakr ibn al-Mundhir said: The general body of scholars agreed that whoever slanders the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) is killed. Among those who said that are Malik, al-Layth, Ahmad, and Ishaq, and it is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i. And his repentance is not accepted according to these, and Abu Hanifa and his companions, al-Thawri, the people of Kufa, and al-Awza'i said the same regarding the Muslim, but they said: it is apostasy. And al-Walid ibn Muslim narrated similarly from Malik, and al-Tabari narrated similarly from Abu Hanifa and his companions regarding one who disparages him (the Prophet) or disavows him or denies him. This ends the quotation from the author of al-Manh. But he said after what will come from al-Jawhara regarding slandering the two shaykhs: I say: the view of not accepting the repentance of one who slanders the Master of the Noble Law is strong, and it is what should be relied upon in giving fatwa and judgment, out of reverence for the Master of the Message, who is specifically endowed with complete virtue and valor. There is discussion in it that you know, and I have investigated the matter in Tanqih al-Hamidiyya, so refer to it. Then I compiled a book on that called Tanbih al-Wulat wa al-Hukkam 'ala Ahkam Shatim Khayr al-Anam aw Ahad Ashabihi al-Kiram, and I explained therein that the statement of al-Shifa 'but they said it is apostasy' etc. is explicit in accepting his repentance, because it is an istidrak (qualification) on his earlier statement 'he is killed and his repentance is not accepted according to these'; so it is known that his statement 'and the like was said by Abu Hanifa' means he said he is killed but they said it is apostasy, so the sum is that he is killed if he does not repent, as is the ruling of apostasy, otherwise the aforementioned istidrak would have no benefit. And among those who explicitly stated acceptance of his repentance according to us is Imam al-Subki in al-Sayf al-Maslul, and he said that this is the madhhab of the people of Kufa and Malik, and he narrated from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. And there is no difference between one who comes repenting on his own or one against whom it is testified, unlike others of the takfir matters, for denial in them is repentance, so testimony does not operate with him, until they said: he is killed even if he slanders while drunk, and there is no pardon, and it must be restricted to when his drunkenness is due to a prohibited cause that he committed willingly without coercion, otherwise he is like a madman. Al-Khattabi said: I do not know anyone who disagreed about the obligation of killing him; as for the like of that regarding Allah, his repentance is accepted to drop his killing. And al-Bazzazi reasoned it as a right with which the right of the servant is attached, so it is not dropped by repentance like other rights of humans, and like the hadd of slander does not go away with repentance, and he explicitly stated that slandering any of the prophets is likewise. And his statement in Fath al-Qadir 'in dropping the killing' indicates that his repentance is accepted with Allah, and it is explicit.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling on an apostate who slanders the Prophet (saw). The author begins by stating that generally there is no distinction between one apostasy and another, but makes an exception for certain cases, the first being slandering the Prophet. According to the Hanafi madhhab, slandering the Prophet constitutes apostasy (ridda) and the culprit is killed as a fixed punishment (hadd). The key point of contention is whether his repentance (tawba) is accepted to drop the execution. The text quotes Fath al-Qadir stating that repentance does not prevent the killing, but then presents a lengthy discussion from various Hanafi sources (Manh al-Ghaffar, al-Bazzaziyya, al-Shifa, etc.) revealing a difference of opinion. Some Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Subki, the author of Tanbih al-Wulat) hold that repentance is accepted, citing that the classification as 'ridda' implies acceptance of tawba (as for any apostate), while others (e.g., the author of Fath al-Qadir, al-Bazzazi) argue that because a right of the servant (haqq al-'abd) is involved—like the hadd of qadhf—repentance does not nullify the punishment. The author of Bahr al-Raiq inclines toward the view that repentance is accepted, as clarified in his own treatise. The passage also clarifies that the slanderer is killed even if he comes repenting voluntarily, and even if he slanders while drunk (provided the drunkenness was from a prohibited cause). The ruling is specific to slandering the Prophet; for slanders against Allah, repentance is accepted.

Key Terms
ردة (ridda): Apostasy from Islam; the legal state of a Muslim who renounces the religion.
ساب (sabb): One who insults or slanders, specifically the Prophet (saw) in this context.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law, in this case execution for slandering the Prophet.
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): A right of a human being or servant, which in this context means the right of the Prophet (saw) that cannot be waived by the criminal's repentance.
استدراك (istidrak): A qualification or correction in a text, where an earlier assertion is refined or limited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position in this text, what happens to a person who slanders the Prophet (saw) and then repents?
A) His repentance is accepted and he is set free.
B) He is killed because the hadd punishment is not dropped by repentance.
C) He is given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir) instead.
D) He is only imprisoned until he shows genuine repentance.

Key Takeaway
Slandering the Prophet carries a fixed hadd of killing that is not nullified by the offender's repentance, because it involves a right of the servant analogous to qadhf.

Slandering the Two Shaykhs: Repentance Accepted or Not?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on repentance acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on whether repentance is accepted for apostasy caused by slandering Abu Bakr and Umar, and state the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Slandering Abu Bakr and Umar is treated like slandering the Prophet—repentance is not accepted.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person commits apostasy by slandering the two Shaykhs, can their repentance save them from execution? The text presents the relied-upon view that it cannot, drawing an analogy with slandering the Prophet. Understanding this ruling is essential for grasping the Hanafi stance on hudud and the inviolability of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on slandering the two Shaykhs
First, note that the act of slandering Abu Bakr and Umar is kufr and requires the death penalty. The question is whether repentance can waive this punishment.
The ruling is based on the inviolability of the Companions.
2
Identify the internal disagreement on repentance
Early sources like al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya do not explicitly discuss acceptance; al-Jawhara raises the issue. Some Hanafis may hold that repentance is accepted by default, but the text focuses on the opposing view.
The disagreement is only about acceptance of repentance, not the act being kufr.
3
Trace the qiyas behind the chosen view
The chosen view (al-Sadr al-Shahid, Abu al-Layth, al-Dabusi) analogizes to slandering the Prophet: after testimony, denial does not constitute repentance. Similarly, slandering the two Shaykhs is like slandering the Prophet, so repentance is futile.
The qiyas is explicit in the passage: 'سب الشيخين كسب النبي'.
4
Evaluate the tarjih and its authority
The author declares the non-acceptance view as 'al-mukhtar li al-fatwa' based on these later authorities. This is a post-classical tarjih, not from the zahir al-riwayah.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.
5
Apply the ruling to a case
If someone slanders both Shaykhs and then repents and renews Islam, they are nonetheless executed. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
There is no lesser punishment; the hadd is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية الردة بسب الشيخين أبي بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما وقد صرح في الخلاصة والبزازية بأن الرافضي إذا سب الشيخين وطعن فيهما كفر، وإن فضل علياً عليهما ،فمبتدع ولم يتكلما على عدم قبول توبته. وفي الجوهرة : من سب الشيخين أو طعن فيهما كفر ويجب قتله، ثم إن رجع وتاب وجدد الإسلام هل تقبل توبته أم لا ؟ قال الصدر الشهيد لا تقبل توبته وإسلامه ونقتله وبه أخذ الفقيه أبو الليث السمرقندي وأبو نصر الدبوسي وهو المختار للفتوى اهـ. وحيث لا تقبل توبته علم أن سب الشيخين لكسب بها النبي الله فلا يفيد الإنكار مع البينة كما تقدم عن فتح القدير لأنا نجعل إنكار الردة توبة إن كانت مقبولة كما لا يخفى
Second: Apostasy by slandering the two shaykhs, Abu Bakr and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them). It has been explicitly stated in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya that the Rafidi, if he slanders the two shaykhs and attacks them, becomes an unbeliever, and if he gives priority to Ali over them, he is an innovator, and they did not discuss refusal to accept his repentance. And in al-Jawhara: Whoever slanders the two shaykhs or attacks them becomes an unbeliever and it is obligatory to kill him. Then if he returns, repents, and renews Islam, is his repentance accepted or not? Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: His repentance and his Islam are not accepted, and we kill him. And this was adopted by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi and Abu Nasr al-Dabusi, and it is the chosen view for fatwa. And since his repentance is not accepted, it is known that slandering the two shaykhs is akin to slandering the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), so denial in the presence of evidence does not avail, as has preceded from Fath al-Qadir, for we make denial of apostasy a repentance only if it is accepted, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage addresses the second exception to the general rule of apostasy: slandering the two Shaykhs, Abu Bakr and Umar (رضي الله عنهما). The text presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether repentance is accepted in this case. It first notes that al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya state that a Rafidi (a Shiite who reviles the Companions) who slanders the two Shaykhs commits kufr, but they do not explicitly discuss acceptance of repentance. The author then quotes al-Jawhara, which states that such a person must be killed, but raises the question of repentance. Al-Sadr al-Shahid, followed by Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi and Abu Nasr al-Dabusi, holds that repentance is not accepted and the culprit is killed. This is the chosen view for fatwa (al-mukhtar li al-fatwa). The passage then explains that slandering the two Shaykhs is treated similarly to slandering the Prophet (saw) in that denial (inkar) after witnesses testify does not constitute repentance that saves him, because in cases where repentance is accepted, denial would be considered repentance. But here, since repentance is not accepted, denial does not help him. This ruling is specific to slandering the two Shaykhs; it does not apply to other types of kufr where repentance is accepted.

Key Terms
رافضي (rafidi): A term for a Shiite who reviles the Companions, especially Abu Bakr and Umar, and may prefer Ali over them.
الشيخين (al-shaykhayn): The two Shaykhs, honorific for Abu Bakr and Umar, the first two caliphs. Slandering them is considered major kufr.
مبتدع (mubtadi'): An innovator in religion; here, one who gives priority to Ali over Abu Bakr and Umar but does not slander them directly is considered a mubtadi', not a kafir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view for fatwa in this passage, what is the ruling on a person who slanders Abu Bakr and Umar (رضي الله عنهما) and then repents?
A) His repentance is accepted and he is set free.
B) He is killed because his repentance is not accepted.
C) He is given a discretionary punishment (ta'zir).
D) He is fined and imprisoned.

Key Takeaway
Slandering the two Shaykhs is an unforgivable apostasy in Hanafi law; the death penalty is carried out regardless of repentance.

Ruling on the Zindiq and Acceptance of Repentance
Explanation of the ruling on Zindiq and the exceptions to the general rule of non-acceptance of repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Zindiq's repentance and identify the exception where it is accepted.

Core Idea
The Zindiq's repentance is generally not accepted unless he comes voluntarily before capture.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on the Zindiq – one who has no religion – and the related hypocrite (munafiq). The apparent madhhab holds that their repentance is not accepted, but a crucial exception applies when the Zindiq voluntarily confesses and repents before being discovered. We will analyze the definitions, the rationale for non-acceptance, and the later fatwa that provides the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Define the key terms
Identify who is a Zindiq (one with no religion) and who is a munafiq (conceals disbelief while outwardly Muslim). Note the distinction: the Zindiq is a heretic/atheist, the munafiq is a hypocrite.
Both are treated similarly in the ruling on repentance.
2
State the apparent madhhab ruling
According to the apparent (zahir) madhhab, the repentance of a Zindiq is not accepted. Understand the reason: lack of confidence in his sincerity because he can easily hide his disbelief.
3
Analyze the exception for voluntary confession
Learn the exception from al-Khaniyya: if the Zindiq comes before being caught, admits his state, and repents, his repentance is accepted. This is supported by Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Taymiyya.
The exception applies only if he is not yet apprehended.
4
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The later Hanafi fatwa (mufta bihi) accepts repentance in the voluntary confession scenario. The text favors this view, as it avoids unnecessary execution and aligns with general principles of accepting repentance from disbelievers who openly repent.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf resolved by later authorities.
5
Apply the distinction to a parallel case
Consider a person who internally denies a necessary matter (e.g., the prohibition of wine) but outwardly affirms it. His repentance is accepted if he returns to the correct belief, similar to the Zindiq who manifests disbelief and then repents.
This highlights the principle: if the disbelief is internal and hidden, repentance is not trusted unless revealed voluntarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالثة لا تقبل توبة الزنديق في ظاهر المذهب وهو من لا يتدين بدين وأما من يبطن الكفر والعياذ بالله تعالى ويظهر الإسلام فهو المنافق ويجب أن يكون حكمه في عدم قبولنا توبته كالزنديق لأن ذلك في الزنديق لعدم الاطمئنان إلى ما يظهر من التوبة إذا كان قد يخفى كفره الذي هو عدم اعتقاده ديناً والمنافق مثله في الإخفاء، وعلى هذا فطريق العلم بحاله إما بأن يعثر بعض الناس عليه أو يسره إلى من إن أمن إليه، والحق أن الذي يقتل ولا تقبل توبته هو المنافق فالزنديق إن كان حكمه ذلك فيجب أن يكون مبطناً كفره الذي هو عدم التدين بدين ويظهر تدينه بالإسلام أو غيره إلى أن ظفرنا به وهو عربي وإلا لو فرضناه مظهراً لذلك حتى تاب يجب أن لا يقتل وتقبل توبته كسائر الكفار المظهرين لكفرهم إذا أظهروا التوبة وكذا من علم أنه ينكر في الباطن بعض الضروريات كحرمة الخمر ويظهر اعتقاد حرمته ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الخانية قالوا : إن جاء الزنديق قبل أن يؤخذ فأقر أنه زنديق فتاب عن ذلك تقبل توبته وإن لم يجد للحنفية إلا قبول التوبة وسبقه إلى ذلك أيضاً شيخ الإسلام ابن تيمية الحنبلي في كتابه الصارم المسلول فصرح فيه في عدة مواضع بقبول التوبة عند الحنفية وأنه لا يقتل قوله : (وفي الجوهرة من سب الشيخين الخ) قال في النهر : هذا لا وجود له في أصل الجوهرة وإنما وجد على هامش بعض النسخ فالحق بالأصل مع أنه لا ارتباط له مع ما قبله.
Third: The repentance of the Zindiq is not accepted in the apparent madhhab. He is one who follows no religion. As for one who conceals disbelief and outwardly manifests Islam, he is the hypocrite (munafiq). His ruling regarding our non-acceptance of his repentance must be like that of the Zindiq, because that ruling for the Zindiq is due to lack of confidence in what appears of repentance when he might hide his disbelief, which is his non-belief in any religion. The hypocrite is similar in concealment. Therefore, the way to know his state is either that some people stumble upon him or he reveals it to someone he trusts. The truth is that the one who is killed and whose repentance is not accepted is the hypocrite. As for the Zindiq, if his ruling is that, he must be one who conceals his disbelief, which is non-adherence to any religion, and manifests adherence to Islam or something else until we apprehend him, and he is an Arab. Otherwise, if we suppose him manifesting that until he repents, he must not be killed and his repentance is accepted, like other disbelievers who manifest their disbelief if they show repentance. Similarly, one who is known to deny in his heart some necessary things like the prohibition of wine but outwardly manifests belief in its prohibition. Thus it is in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Khaniyya they said: If the Zindiq comes before being caught and admits that he is a Zindiq and repents from that, his repentance is accepted. And there is no escape for the Hanafis except acceptance of repentance, and Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Taymiyya al-Hanbali preceded him in that in his book al-Sarim al-Maslul, for he explicitly stated in several places that repentance is accepted according to the Hanafis and that he is not killed. His statement: (And in al-Jawhara: whoever slanders the two Shaykhs etc.) said in al-Nahr: This does not exist in the original of al-Jawhara; rather it was found in the margin of some copies, so it is attached to the original, and it has no connection with what precedes it.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage addresses the third exception: the Zindiq, defined as one who follows no religion at all. The apparent (zahir) madhhab is that his repentance is not accepted. The author then distinguishes between a Zindiq and a hypocrite (munafiq), who conceals disbelief and outwardly appears Muslim. The ruling for the hypocrite is similar: his repentance is not accepted until his condition is known through discovery or confession. However, the text clarifies that the truth (al-haqq) is that the one who is killed and whose repentance is not accepted is the hypocrite. As for the Zindiq, if he is an Arab who conceals his disbelief and manifests Islam, his repentance is not accepted. But if he manifests his disbelief (i.e., openly declares he has no religion) and then repents, his repentance is accepted, similar to other disbelievers. The same applies to one who internally denies a necessary matter of religion (e.g., the prohibition of wine) but outwardly affirms it—his repentance is accepted if he returns to the correct belief. The passage then provides a crucial exception from al-Khaniyya: if a Zindiq comes voluntarily before being captured, admits his state, and repents, his repentance is accepted. The author notes that the Hanafi madhhab essentially accepts repentance in such cases, and this is supported by Ibn Taymiyya. A final note criticizes a marginal addition in al-Jawhara regarding slandering the two Shaykhs, stating it is not part of the original text and is unrelated.

Key Terms
زنديق (zindiq): One who has no religion (dīn), i.e., an atheist or heretic who believes in nothing.
منافق (munafiq): A hypocrite who conceals disbelief and outwardly shows Islam. His ruling is similar to the Zindiq in that repentance is not accepted unless discovered.
ظاهر المذهب (zahir al-madhhab): The apparent or well-known position of the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because he is a disbeliever and disbelievers cannot repent.
B) Because there is no confidence in the sincerity of his repentance due to his ability to conceal disbelief.
C) Because he is not considered a Muslim even after repentance.
D) Because the punishment for zandaqah is death regardless.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab generally does not accept the Zindiq's repentance, but an exception exists if he voluntarily confesses and repents before capture.

Execution of Apostate Despite Repentance
Ruling on apostate repentance with proof from Abu Bakr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on apostate repentance, explain the proof from Abu Bakr, and distinguish the rationale based on human rights.

Core Idea
Apostasy incurs a human right, so repentance does not avert execution in this world.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that an apostate must be executed even if he sincerely repents. We will trace the proof from the practice of Abu Bakr and understand the legal rationale distinguishing rights of Allah from rights of humans. A nuanced exception exists for blasphemy against Allah, where repentance is accepted to waive execution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling on apostate repentance
Find the explicit statement in the text: the apostate is killed even if he repents, whether he comes voluntarily or after testimony.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The text cites the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq as evidence. Recognize this as a Qawl Sahabi (saying of a Companion) for the Hanafi school.
The dalil is considered zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala in this context.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The text explains that apostasy involves a human right (haqq al-'abd), so it is not dropped by repentance, analogous to hadd al-qadhf. Contrast with rights of Allah.
Al-Bazzazi's explanation is cited to clarify this distinction.
4
Note the exception for blasphemy against Allah
The text states that for blasphemy against Allah (sabb Allah), repentance is accepted to waive execution, because it is a right of Allah. For blasphemy against prophets, the same ruling as apostasy applies.
Al-Khattabi notes consensus on the obligation to kill the apostate, but an exception is made for direct blasphemy against Allah.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
Though the Hanafi school holds this ruling, some other scholars do not execute a repentant apostate. Identify that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The text indicates that the madhhab of Kufa and Malik agrees, but others differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن هذا مذهب أهل الكوفة ومالك، ونقل عن أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه . ولا فرق بين يجيء تائباً . من نفسه أو شهد عليه بذلك بخلاف غيره من المكفرات فإن الإنكار فيها توبة فلا تعمل الشهادة معه حتى قالوا يقتل وإن سب سكران ولا يعفى عنه ولا بد من تقييده بما إذا كان سكره بسبب محظور باشره مختاراً بلا إكراه وإلا فهو كالمجنون. قال الخطابي : لا أعلم أحداً خالف في وجوب قتله وأما مثله في حقه تعالى فتقبل توبته في إسقاط قتله اهـ. وعلله البزازي بأنه حق تعلق به حق العبد فلا يسقط بالتوبة كسائر حقوق الآدميين وكحد القذف لا يزول بالتوبة، وصرح بأن سب واحد من الأنبياء كذلك. وقوله في فتح القدير في إسقاط القتل يفيد أن توبته مقبولة عند الله تعالى وهو مصرح به.
Indeed, this is the madhhab of the people of Kufa and Malik, and it is transmitted from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him. And there is no difference between one who comes repenting of his own accord and one against whom testimony is established, contrary to other types of kufr, for in those denial is repentance, so testimony is not effective with it, so they said: He is killed even if he blasphemes while drunk, and he is not pardoned. And it is necessary to qualify it with the condition that his drunkenness was due to a prohibited cause that he undertook voluntarily without coercion, otherwise he is like an insane person. Al-Khattabi said: I do not know of anyone who disagreed on the obligation to kill him. As for his like in the case of Allah the Exalted, his repentance is accepted to waive his execution. End. And al-Bazzazi explained it by saying that it is a right that involves the right of a human being, so it is not dropped by repentance, like other human rights and like the hadd punishment for slander which is not removed by repentance. And he stated that blasphemy against any of the prophets is the same. And his statement in Fath al-Qadir about waiving execution indicates that his repentance is accepted in the sight of Allah the Exalted, and this is explicitly stated.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the commentary Al-Bahr al-Raiq on the chapter of apostates. It presents the Hanafi position that an apostate is executed even if he repents, citing the practice of Abu Bakr and the madhhab of the Kufans and Malik. The ruling distinguishes apostasy from other types of kufr where denial is considered repentance. The execution applies also to a drunk blasphemer if his drunkenness was voluntarily from a prohibited cause. Al-Khattabi affirms consensus on the obligation to kill the apostate. However, for blasphemy directly against Allah, repentance is accepted to avert execution, though the worldly punishment remains for apostasy because it involves a human right (related to the community). This is analogized to hadd for qadhf. The passage also notes that blasphemy against any prophet has the same ruling. Fath al-Qadir confirms that repentance is accepted in the sight of Allah but does not stop the execution.

Key Terms
ردة (riddah): Apostasy; a Muslim's abandonment of Islam.
سب (sabb): Insult or blasphemy against Allah, prophets, or companions.
توبة (tawbah): Repentance; for apostasy, it does not avert execution in this world.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on an apostate who repents before being captured?
A) He is pardoned and not executed.
B) He is executed even if he repents.
C) He is imprisoned until he proves sincerity.
D) He is exiled.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that apostasy involves a human right, so repentance does not prevent execution, unlike acts that are solely rights of Allah.

Repentance of Zindiq and Munafiq in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling with intra-madhhab variance on acceptance of repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting the repentance of a zindiq and munafiq, and distinguish between the cases of capture and voluntary surrender.

Core Idea
The repentance of a zindiq or munafiq is not accepted after capture because their inner state remains concealed.

This lesson examines the ruling on the repentance of those who conceal their disbelief (zindiq and munafiq). The Hanafi school distinguishes between those captured and those who voluntarily come forward. Understanding this principle is crucial for applying hudud correctly.

Guided Path
1
Define the terms
Identify the meanings of 'zindiq' (one who adheres to no religion) and 'munafiq' (one who conceals disbelief and outwardly shows Islam). Both are similar in that they hide their true beliefs.
The key is concealment – their inner state is unknown to others.
2
State the general rule
According to the apparent Hanafi madhhab (zahir al-riwaya), the repentance of a captured zindiq or munafiq is not accepted and he is executed.
This is because their outward repentance cannot be trusted due to their habitual concealment.
3
Identify the exception
If the zindiq voluntarily comes forward before being captured, admits his state, and repents, his repentance is accepted (as per al-Khaniya).
Voluntary admission suggests sincerity, unlike belated repentance after capture.
4
Note the legal reasoning
The Hanafi rationale: there is no assurance (itmi'nan) that the repentance is genuine because the inner kufr was hidden. This applies to both zindiq and munafiq.
For those who openly manifest kufr like regular apostates, repentance is accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالثة لا تقبل توبة الزنديق في ظاهر المذهب وهو من لا يتدين بدين وأما من يبطن الكفر والعياذ بالله تعالى ويظهر الإسلام فهو المنافق ويجب أن يكون حكمه في عدم قبولنا توبته كالزنديق لأن ذلك في الزنديق لعدم الاطمئنان إلى ما يظهر من التوبة إذا كان قد يخفى كفره الذي هو عدم اعتقاده ديناً والمنافق مثله في الإخفاء، وعلى هذا فطريق العلم بحاله إما بأن يعثر بعض الناس عليه أو يسره إلى من إن أمن إليه، والحق أن الذي يقتل ولا تقبل توبته هو المنافق فالزنديق إن كان حكمه ذلك فيجب أن يكون مبطناً كفره الذي هو عدم التدين بدين ويظهر تدينه بالإسلام أو غيره إلى أن ظفرنا به وهو عربي وإلا لو فرضناه مظهراً لذلك حتى تاب يجب أن لا يقتل وتقبل توبته كسائر الكفار المظهرين لكفرهم إذا أظهروا التوبة وكذا من علم أنه ينكر في الباطن بعض الضروريات كحرمة الخمر ويظهر اعتقاد حرمته ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي الخانية قالوا : إن جاء الزنديق قبل أن يؤخذ فأقر أنه زنديق فتاب عن ذلك تقبل توبته وإن لم يجد للحنفية إلا قبول التوبة وسبقه إلى ذلك أيضاً شيخ الإسلام ابن تيمية الحنبلي في كتابه الصارم المسلول فصرح فيه في عدة مواضع بقبول التوبة عند الحنفية وأنه لا يقتل قوله : (وفي الجوهرة من سب الشيخين الخ) قال في النهر : هذا لا وجود له في أصل الجوهرة وإنما وجد على هامش بعض النسخ فالحق بالأصل مع أنه لا ارتباط له مع ما قبله. أخذ ثم تاب لم تقبل توبته ويقتل .اهـ.
The third [type]: the repentance of the zindiq is not accepted in the apparent madhhab, and he is one who follows no religion. As for one who conceals disbelief and outwardly shows Islam, he is the munafiq, and his ruling regarding our non-acceptance of his repentance must be like the zindiq, because that is in the zindiq due to lack of assurance in what appears of repentance, since he may hide his kufr which is his non-belief in any religion, and the munafiq is similar in concealment. Based on this, the way to know his condition is either by some people discovering him or he reveals it to someone he trusts. The truth is that the one who is killed and whose repentance is not accepted is the munafiq. As for the zindiq, if his ruling is that, then he must be one who conceals his kufr (which is non-adherence to any religion) and outwardly shows adherence to Islam or other until we capture him, and he is an Arab; otherwise, if we assume him to be outwardly [showing his kufr] such that he repents, then he must not be killed and his repentance is accepted, like other disbelievers who openly show their kufr when they show repentance. Similarly, one who is known to inwardly deny some essentials, like the prohibition of wine, and outwardly shows belief in its prohibition; as in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Khaniya they said: If the zindiq comes before being captured and admits that he is a zindiq and then repents from that, his repentance is accepted. And they did not find for the Hanafis except acceptance of repentance, and Shaykh al-Islam Ibn Taymiyya al-Hanbali preceded them in that in his book al-Sarim al-Maslul, where he stated in several places the acceptance of repentance among the Hanafis and that he is not killed. His statement: (And in al-Jawhara about insulting the two Shaykhs, etc.) said in al-Nahr: This does not exist in the original al-Jawhara; it was only found on the margin of some copies, so it should be attributed to the original, and there is no connection with what precedes it. He was captured and then repented, his repentance is not accepted and he is killed. End.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage discusses the third category: the zindiq (one who follows no religion) and the munafiq (hypocrite who hides disbelief and shows Islam). According to the apparent madhhab, their repentance is not accepted because their inner state is unknown, so their outward show of repentance cannot be trusted. However, there is a detail: if the zindiq openly manifests his disbelief and then repents, his repentance is accepted like that of any other open disbeliever. The same applies to one who secretly denies an essential of religion but outwardly claims belief. The Khaniya reports that if the zindiq comes forward voluntarily and admits his state before being captured, his repentance is accepted. This is also supported by Ibn Taymiyya. The marginal note about al-Jawhara clarifies that a statement regarding insulting the two Shaykhs that was attributed to it is spurious. The passage ends by reiterating that if he is captured and then repents, it is not accepted.

Key Terms
زنديق (zindīq): One who does not adhere to any religion, often a heretic.
منافق (munāfiq): Hypocrite who conceals disbelief and outwardly shows Islam.
ضروريات الدين (ḍarūriyyāt al-dīn): Essentials of religion; denying them constitutes kufr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His repentance is accepted and he is not killed.
B) His repentance is not accepted and he is killed.
C) He is given a period to prove sincerity.
D) He is exiled.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the repentance of a zindiq or munafiq is not accepted after capture due to the unreliability of their concealed state, but voluntary surrender before capture allows acceptance.

Repentance of the Sorcerer: Types and Timing
Ruling on sorcerer's repentance with categories based on belief and timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the different categories of sorcerers and state the Hanafi ruling on their repentance and execution.

Core Idea
A sorcerer's repentance is accepted only if he abandons false belief or repents before capture; after capture, execution proceeds.

In this passage, the author examines the ruling on a sorcerer's repentance, showing that not all sorcerers are treated the same. The key factor is what the sorcerer believed about his actions and when he repented. We will explore the classifications from Fath al-Qadir and al-Khaniya, and the relied-upon view of Abu al-Layth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the sorcerer's repentance (tawbah) and the legal consequence (execution or not). Determine if the repentance is accepted and whether execution is wajib.
2
Distinguish categories based on belief
Three categories are mentioned: sorcerer who believed himself a creator, experimental sorcerer (no belief in effect), and a denier who practices without knowledge. Each has a different ruling.
Belief is the key factor for the first category.
3
Apply the timing distinction
According to Abu al-Layth, repentance before capture is accepted; after capture it is not, and execution follows.
This is the mufta bihi view.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Fath al-Qadir equates the sorcerer to the zindiq (repentance not accepted), while al-Khaniya and Abu al-Layth provide a more nuanced view.
The later preferred view is Abu al-Layth's.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text explicitly states 'the fatwa is upon this statement' referring to Abu al-Layth's view.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابعة توبة الساحر جعله في فتح القدير كالزنديق لا تقبل توبته. وفي الخانية من كتاب الخطر والإباحة: الساحر إذا تاب فهو على وجوه : إن كان يعتقد نفسه خالقاً لما يفعل فإن تاب عن ذلك فقال خالق كل شيء هو الله تعالى وتبرأ عما كان يقول تقبل توبته ولا يقتل وإن كان الساحر يستعمل السحر بالتجربة والامتحان ولا يعتقد لذلك أثراً لا بكافر. وساحر يجحد السحر ولا يدري كيف يفعل ولا يقربه قالوا : لا يستتاب بل يقتل إذا ثبت أنه يستعمل السحر، وفي بعض المواضع ذكر أن الاستتابة أحوط. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث : إذا تاب الساحر قبل أن يؤخذ تقبل توبته ولا يقتل وإن أخذ ثم تاب لم تقبل توبته ويقتل، وكذا الزنديق المعروف الداعي والفتوى على هذا القول اهـ .
The fourth [type]: repentance of the sorcerer. In Fath al-Qadir, he is made like the zindiq; his repentance is not accepted. And in al-Khaniya from the book al-Khatr wa al-Ibaha: The sorcerer, if he repents, has aspects: If he believed himself to be the creator of what he does, then repents from that, saying 'The Creator of everything is Allah the Exalted' and disavows what he used to say, his repentance is accepted and he is not killed. And if the sorcerer uses sorcery through experience and testing, and does not believe it has any effect, he is not a disbeliever. And a sorcerer who denies sorcery and does not know how it is done and does not practice it, they said: He is not called to repent but is killed if it is established that he practices sorcery. In some places it is mentioned that calling to repentance (isti’tab) is more cautious. And the jurist Abu al-Layth said: If the sorcerer repents before being captured, his repentance is accepted and he is not killed; if he is captured and then repents, his repentance is not accepted and he is killed. Likewise the zindiq known for calling [to his beliefs], and the fatwa is upon this statement. End.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth category: the sorcerer's repentance. Fath al-Qadir equates him with the zindiq, generally not accepting repentance. However, al-Khaniya provides a detailed classification: if the sorcerer believed himself to be a creator and then repents from that, his repentance is accepted. If he merely uses sorcery experimentally without believing in its effect, he is not a disbeliever. A sorcerer who denies sorcery but practices it is not given the opportunity to repent but is killed. Abu al-Layth distinguishes based on timing: if he repents before capture, it is accepted; after capture, it is not. This is also applied to the well-known preaching zindiq, and this is the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Key Terms
ساحر (sāḥir): Sorcerer; one who practices magic.
استتابة (istitābah): Calling a person to repent before execution.
خطر وإباحة (khaṭr wa ibāḥah): A Hanafi fiqh source (Kitab al-Khatr wa al-Ibaha) addressing permissibility and prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If he never believed in his sorcery.
B) If he repents before being captured.
C) If he repents after capture.
D) His repentance is never accepted.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between sorcerers based on belief and timing of repentance, and the fatwa follows Abu al-Layth's view.

Repentance of the Sorcerer and Zindiq
Ruling on the repentance of a sorcerer and zindiq with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on accepting the repentance of a sorcerer and identify the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding the timing of repentance.

Core Idea
For a sorcerer, repentance before capture is accepted; after capture it is not — this is the mufta bihi.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between types of sorcerers and the timing of their repentance. While some earlier Hanafis rejected repentance entirely, the relied-upon view (after Abu al-Layth) accepts it only if done before capture. This lesson unpacks the classification and the underlying reasons.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main issue
What is the ruling on the repentance of a sorcerer? The passage discusses whether his repentance is accepted and whether he is killed.
The issue centers on capital punishment for sorcery.
2
List the different positions within the Hanafi school
Some earlier Hanafis (e.g., in Fath al-Qadir) treat the sorcerer like a zindiq, never accepting repentance. Others, like Abu al-Layth, distinguish based on timing.
The text presents multiple views from al-Khaniyyah and Fath al-Qadir.
3
Understand the basis for each position
The key distinction is whether the sorcerer believes himself to be a creator (kufr) or merely practices sorcery experimentally (not kufr). This affects the ruling.
Belief in self-creation makes him a disbeliever; repentance from that is accepted if sincere.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a sorcerer who repents before capture is not killed and is considered a Muslim; one who repents after capture is still executed.
Timing of repentance thus directly determines life or death.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its authority
The text states 'al-fatwa ala hadha al-qawl' (the fatwa is on this opinion), referring to Abu al-Layth's distinction. This is the relied-upon view for both the sorcerer and the active zindiq.
Authority: Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, from later Hanafi works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخذ ثم تاب لم تقبل توبته ويقتل .اهـ. وتفصيل حسن موافق لما بحثه في فتح القدير هو الرابعة توبة الساحر جعله في فتح القدير كالزنديق لا تقبل توبته. وفي الخانية من كتاب الخطر والإباحة: الساحر إذا تاب فهو على وجوه : إن كان يعتقد نفسه خالقاً لما يفعل فإن تاب عن ذلك فقال خالق كل شيء هو الله تعالى وتبرأ عما كان يقول تقبل توبته ولا يقتل وإن كان الساحر يستعمل السحر بالتجربة والامتحان ولا يعتقد لذلك أثراً لا بكافر. وساحر يجحد السحر ولا يدري كيف يفعل ولا يقربه قالوا : لا يستتاب بل يقتل إذا ثبت أنه يستعمل السحر، وفي بعض المواضع ذكر أن الاستتابة أحوط. وقال الفقيه أبو الليث : إذا تاب الساحر قبل أن يؤخذ تقبل توبته ولا يقتل وإن أخذ ثم تاب لم تقبل توبته ويقتل، وكذا الزنديق المعروف الداعي والفتوى على هذا القول اهـ .
He took [the sorcerer], then he repented: his repentance is not accepted and he is killed. There is a detailed, good opinion consistent with what was researched in Fath al-Qadir: it is the fourth [type]: repentance of the sorcerer. He made it in Fath al-Qadir like the zindiq: his repentance is not accepted. In al-Khaniyyah, from the book of al-Khatar wa al-Ibahah: The sorcerer, when he repents, is of several types: If he believed himself to be the creator of what he does, then repents from that saying, 'The Creator of everything is Allah Almighty,' and disavows what he used to say, his repentance is accepted and he is not killed. If the sorcerer uses sorcery by experimentation and examination and does not believe it has any effect, he is not a disbeliever. And a sorcerer who denies sorcery and does not know how it is done and does not practice it—they said: he is not asked to repent but is killed, when it is established that he used sorcery. And in some places it is mentioned that asking for repentance is more cautious. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: If the sorcerer repents before being captured, his repentance is accepted and he is not killed. If he is captured then repents, his repentance is not accepted and he is killed. Likewise the well-known zindiq who calls to his belief—the fatwa is according to this opinion.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra‘iq discusses the ruling on accepting the repentance of a sorcerer (sahir) and a zindiq (heretic). The author first mentions that some hold any repentance after capture is unacceptable, then provides a detailed classification. The central Hanafi position, as in Fath al-Qadir, equates the sorcerer with the zindiq in certain cases—if the sorcerer believes himself to be a creator, he is a disbeliever; if he repents and affirms that Allah alone is Creator, his repentance is accepted. However, if he merely practices sorcery as an experiment without believing in its independent effect, he is not a disbeliever. There is also a view (from Abu al-Layth) that distinguishes between repentance before capture (accepted) and after capture (not accepted). The relied-upon fatwa follows Abu al-Layth for both the sorcerer and the active zindiq. The passage illustrates how Hanafi jurists weigh intention, belief, and timing in determining the validity of repentance and the consequent legal status.

Key Terms
زنديق (zindiq): A heretic who outwardly professes Islam but inwardly holds heretical beliefs and calls others to them.
توبة (tawbah): Repentance from disbelief or sin; legally accepted when it meets conditions (e.g., sincerity, abandoning the sin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Testimony on Apostasy and the Effect of Denial
Ruling on testimony of apostasy and the effect of denial

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of witnesses required for apostasy and explain why denial is treated as repentance, distinguishing between the penal and civil consequences.

Core Idea
Denial of apostasy is legally considered repentance, sparing the accused from execution but not from civil dissolution of marriage.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq clarifies a critical nuance in Hanafi law: when two just witnesses testify against a Muslim for apostasy, the testimony is accepted and the apostasy is established—yet the accused's denial is not ignored. Instead, the denial itself is deemed an act of repentance (tawbah), which aborts capital punishment while still triggering civil effects like nullification of marriage. The author warns against a common error: thinking that denial negates the testimony altogether.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi rule on the number of witnesses for apostasy and the legal treatment of the accused's denial.
The rule is that two just witnesses suffice; denial does not invalidate the testimony.
2
Locate the dissenting view and its proof
Note al-Hasan's opinion requiring four witnesses, analogizing to adultery. Understand why Hanafis reject this qiyas.
Al-Hasan's qiyas is weak in Hanafi usul because the analogy ignores the nature of apostasy as a purely verbal act.
3
Analyze the two legal consequences
Distinguish between the penal consequence (execution) and the civil consequences (marriage dissolution). The denial only affects the former.
Execution is prevented because denial is repentance; civil consequences remain because apostasy is proven.
4
Recognize the common misunderstanding
Understand the error of thinking that denial nullifies the testimony. The author explicitly refutes this.
The misunderstanding arises from conflating 'testimony not effective with denial' with 'testimony not accepted'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتح القدير : وتقبل الشهادة بالردة من عدلين ولا يعلم مخالف إلا الحسن قال : لا يقبل في القتل إلا أربعة قياساً على الزنا، وإذا شهدوا على مسلم بالردة وهو منكر لا يتعرض له لا لتكذيب الشهود العدول بل لأن إنكاره توبة ورجوع .اهـ. وهذا معنى قوله فيما نقلناه آنفاً عنه أن الشهادة لا تعمل مع الإنكار وليس المراد أن ردته لا تثبت بالشهادة مع الإنكار بل تثبت ويحكم بها حتى تبين زوجته منه ويجب تجديد النكاح وإنما يمتنع القتل فقط للتوبة بالإنكار، وقد رأيت من يغلط في هذا المحل.
And in Fath al-Qadir: Testimony of apostasy is accepted from two just witnesses, and there is no known dissenter except al-Hasan, who said: Testimony is not accepted in [cases leading to] killing except [from] four, by analogy to adultery. And if they testify against a Muslim of apostasy while he denies it, he is not to be interfered with—not because the just witnesses are lying, but because his denial is [considered] repentance and return. This is the meaning of his statement we quoted earlier, that testimony is not effective with denial. It is not intended that his apostasy is not established by testimony with denial; rather it is established and a ruling is made accordingly, so that his wife becomes separated from him and renewal of marriage becomes obligatory. But execution is only prevented because of repentance through denial. I have seen people who err in this place.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra‘iq, commenting on Fath al-Qadir, addresses the procedure when testimony of apostasy is brought against a Muslim who denies it. The default Hanafi position is that apostasy is proven by two male witnesses. A minority opinion (al-Hasan) requires four witnesses, analogizing to adultery, but this is not followed. The key point is that if the accused denies the apostasy, the denial itself is considered an act of repentance (tawbah), and thus the capital punishment is averted. However, the apostasy is still legally established: the marital bond is broken, and the couple must renew the marriage if they wish to stay together. The author warns against a common misunderstanding: the denial does not negate the testimony; rather it functions as a retroactive repentance that spares the accused from execution. Thus the testimony is effective in terms of civil consequences (e.g., inheritance, marriage), but not for penal consequences because of the denial-turned-repentance.

Key Terms
إنكار (inkar): Denial by the accused of the allegation of apostasy; legally treated as repentance.
عدل (adl): A just witness, satisfying the conditions of 'adalah (integrity) in Islamic law.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; al-Hasan uses qiyas on zina to require four witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal effect of a Muslim's denial of apostasy after two just witnesses have testified?
A) The testimony is rejected, and the person remains a Muslim without any legal consequences.
B) The apostasy is established, but the denial is considered repentance, preventing execution while civil effects remain.
C) The person is executed immediately because the denial contradicts the testimony.
D) The testimony is accepted only if four witnesses are present, otherwise the denial is ignored.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, denial of apostasy is legally characterized as repentance, which spares the accused from capital punishment but does not nullify the testimony's civil consequences.

Criminal Liability of an Apostate Who Returns to Islam
Detailed ruling on apostate's liability for criminal offenses upon return to Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the liability for hudud (rights of Allah) and huquq al-ibad (rights of individuals) when an apostate returns to Islam, and apply the correct ruling to different scenarios.

Core Idea
Hudud are waived for an apostate who returns, but rights of people (qisas, property) remain.

This passage from al-Khaniyya presents a detailed ruling on the criminal liability of an apostate who later becomes Muslim again. The key principle is that apostasy and subsequent return to Islam wipe out hudud punishments that are pure rights of Allah, but do not affect the rights of individuals, such as qisas and financial guarantees. The ruling also depends on whether the apostate was in Dar al-Harb or in the imam's custody.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of crimes
The text divides crimes into hudud (fixed punishments) and rights of individuals (qisas, property). Recognize which is which in each scenario.
2
Analyze each scenario
For each distinct situation (crimes before apostasy, after apostasy in Dar al-Islam, after joining Dar al-Harb, while in custody), determine whether the apostate is liable upon return.
Pay attention to the location and timing.
3
Apply the overarching principle
Huquq al-ibad persist; hudud are waived unless the apostate is in custody of the imam or the crime involved financial guarantee (as in theft).
The principle is derived from the text's explicit statements.
4
Examine the analogical reasoning
The text draws an analogy (qiyas) between an apostate in Dar al-Harb and a harbi, both are not subject to Islamic law at the time of the crime.
This supports the waiver of hudud for acts committed in Dar al-Harb.

ومنها ما في الخانية: مسلم أصاب مالاً أو شيئاً يجب به القصاص أو حد قذف ثم ارتد وأصاب ذلك وهو مرتد في دار الإسلام ثم لحق بدار الحرب وحارب المسلمين زماناً ثم جاء مسلماً فهو مأخوذ بجميع ذلك، ولو أصاب ذلك بعد ما لحق بدار الحرب مرتداً وأسلم فذلك كله موضوع عنه لأنه أصابه وهو حربي في دار الحرب والحربي لا يؤاخذ بعد الإسلام بما كان أصابه حال كونه محارباً. وما أصاب المسلم من حدود الله تعالى كالزنا والسرقة وقطع الطريق ثم ارتد أو أصاب ذلك بعد الردة ثم لحق بدار الحرب ثم جاء مسلماً فكل ذلك يكون موضوعاً عنه إلا أنه يضمن المال في السرقة، وإذا أصاب دماً في الطريق كان عليه القصاص لأن ما كان من حقوق العباد كان المرتد مأخوذاً بذلك، وما أصاب في قطع الطريق من القتل خطأ ففيه الدية على عاقلته إن أصابه قبل الردة، وفي ماله إن أصابه بعد الردة، وإن وجب على المسلم حد الشرب من الخمر أو المسكر ثم ارتد ثم أسلم قبل اللحوق بدار الحرب فإنه لا يؤاخذ بذلك لأن الكفر يمنع وجوب هذا الحد ابتداء حتى لا يجب على الذمي والمستأمن فإذا اعترض الكفر بعد الوجوب يمنع البقاء، وإن أصاب ذلك والمرتد محبوس في يد الإمام فإنه لا يؤاخذ بحد الخمر والسكر وهو مؤاخذ بما سوى ذلك من حدود الله تعالى، ويتمكن الإمام من إقامة هذا الحد إذا كان في يده، فإن لم يكن في يده حين أصاب ذلك ثم أسلم قبل اللحوق بدار الحرب فذلك موضوع عنه أيضاً اهـ.
Among them is what is in al-Khaniyya: A Muslim acquires wealth or something entailing qisas or the hadd of slander, then apostatizes and acquires that while an apostate in the abode of Islam, then joins the abode of war and fights Muslims for a time, then comes back as a Muslim — he is taken to account for all of that. If he acquired that after joining the abode of war as an apostate and becomes Muslim, all of that is waived for him because he acquired it while being a harbi in the abode of war, and a harbi is not taken to account after Islam for what he acquired while being a combatant. What a Muslim commits of the hudud of Allah, like zina, theft, and highway robbery, then apostatizes, or commits that after apostasy, then joins the abode of war, then comes back as a Muslim — all of that is waived for him, except that he guarantees the property in theft. If he kills someone in highway robbery, qisas is required because what pertains to the rights of people, the apostate is held accountable. If in highway robbery he kills by mistake, the blood money is on his 'aqila if the killing occurred before apostasy, and on his own wealth if after apostasy. If a Muslim is liable for the hadd of drinking wine or intoxicant, then apostatizes, then becomes Muslim before joining the abode of war, he is not taken to account for that because disbelief prevents the obligation of this hadd initially — it is not obligatory on a dhimmi or musta'min; thus if disbelief intervenes after obligation, it prevents persistence. If the apostate commits that while imprisoned by the imam, he is not taken to account for the hadd of wine and intoxicant, but he is taken to account for other hudud of Allah, and the imam can enforce this hadd if he has him in his custody. If he was not in his custody when he committed it, then becomes Muslim before joining the abode of war, that is also waived for him. End quote.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with rational proofs from al-Khaniyya on the criminal liability of an apostate who later returns to Islam. It distinguishes between different scenarios: (1) If the apostasy and crimes occurred in Dar al-Islam and the apostate later joins Dar al-Harb, then returns as Muslim, he is liable for financial crimes, qisas, and hadd of slander, but not for hudud like theft (except property guarantee) and highway robbery. (2) If he acquires wealth or commits crimes after becoming a harbi in Dar al-Harb, he is not liable upon return because as a harbi he was not subject to Islamic law. (3) For hudud like drinking, if apostasy occurs after the obligation but before punishment, the hadd is dropped because disbelief prevents its persistence. However, if the apostate is in the imam's custody, the hadd can still be enforced. The key principle: rights of people (huquq al-ibad) like qisas and financial guarantees remain, while pure rights of Allah (hudud) are waived due to apostasy and subsequent return, especially if the apostate was in dar al-harb.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Allah for specific crimes (e.g., zina, theft, drinking).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or bodily harm; a right of the victim or their heirs.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule with which Muslims are in a state of war.
حقوق العباد (huquq al-ibad): Rights of individuals (e.g., property, life, honor); as opposed to huquq Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a Muslim commits theft (which requires hadd), then apostatizes, joins dar al-harb, and later returns to Islam, what is his liability?
A) He is completely free from any penalty.
B) The hadd of theft is waived, but he must return the stolen property.
C) He must still undergo the hadd of theft.
D) He must compensate the stolen property, and the hadd is also enforced.

Key Takeaway
An apostate who returns to Islam is liable for huquq al-ibad (qisas, property) but not for hudud (unless in custody); apostasy wipes out pure Huquq Allah.

The Harbi Principle: No Accountability for Past Hudud After Islam
Explains forgiveness of hudud for those outside Islamic jurisdiction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a harbi is not held accountable for previous hudud upon embracing Islam, and apply it to the case of an apostate who joins dar al-harb and returns.

Core Idea
A person is not punished for hudud committed outside Islamic jurisdiction, whether as a harbi or an apostate after joining dar al-harb.

This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a foundational principle: Islamic penal law only applies to those under its jurisdiction. The text explains that a harbi (non-Muslim combatant) is not punished for past crimes after embracing Islam, and similarly, an apostate who flees to dar al-harb and later returns as a Muslim is forgiven for all hudud except those involving rights of others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A person commits hadd crimes (zina, theft, highway robbery) while a harbi in dar al-harb, then accepts Islam.
2
State the general principle
The harbi is not held accountable after Islam because he was not under Islamic jurisdiction at the time.
Dalil aqli: jurisdiction-based.
3
Extend to the apostate
A Muslim commits hadd, then apostatizes, flees to dar al-harb, then returns as Muslim. The apostasy and flight place him outside jurisdiction, so hudud are also forgiven.
Exception: property and qisas remain.
4
Identify the exception
The text states that property theft (damān) and intentional homicide (qisas) are not forgiven because they are rights of people (huquq al-‘ibad).
This aligns with the maxim that rights of people are not waived by apostasy.
5
Conclusion
The ruling is based on a rational argument: no jurisdiction means no liability for hudud, but rights of people survive.

الكتاب. وأشار بقوله وإلا قتل إلى أنه لا يجوز استرقاقه وإن لحق بدار الحرب لأنه لم يشرع فيه إلا الإسلام أو السيف. وفي الخانية : لا يترك على ردته بإعطاء الجزية ولا بأمان موقت ولا بأمان مؤبد ولا يجوز استرقاقه بعد اللحاق مرتداً إذا أخذه المسلمون أسيراً، ويجوز استرقاق المرتدة بعد اللحاق .اهـ. ومن أحكامه أنه لا عاقلة له لأنها للمعونة وهو يعاون؛ كذا في البدائع. وقد مضى في باب نكاح الكافر وقوع الفرقة بردة أحد الزوجين وفي المحرمات أنه لا ينكح ولا ينكح وسيأتي أنه لا يرث من أحد لانعدام الملة والولاية فقد ظهر أن الردة أفحش من الكفر الأصلي في الدنيا والآخرة وأطلق في القتل فشمل الحر والعبد فولاية قتل العبد المرتد للإمام لا للمولى لإطلاق النصوص وفي الولوالجية : إذا باع عبده المرتد أو أمته المرتدة جاز والردة عيب لأنه مملوك له فيجوز بيعه وفي حق العبد يوجب استحقاق القتل عليه فيكون عيباً وردة الأمة تفوّت على المشتري منفعة الوطء فيكون عيباً أيضاً اهـ. وفي شرح المجمع معزياً إلى الحقائق : ولا تجالس ولا تواكل ولا تباع اهـ. ويشترط في جواز قتل المرتد أن لا يكون إسلامه بطريق التبعية ولذا قال في البدائع أقر بالإسلام ثم ارتد يقتل ولكنه في الأولى يحبس لأنه كان له حكم الإسلام قبل تحقيقه والله أعلم. ثم لا يخفى أن هذا كله في غير الذي يطالب بأدائه بعد الإسلام كحقوق العباد وقضاء ما تركه من صلاة وصيام .
The book of Siyar / Chapter of rulings of apostates. All that is forgiven because it afflicted him while he was a harbi in dar al-harb, and the harbi is not held accountable after Islam for what afflicted him while being a combatant. Whatever a Muslim incurs of the hudud of Allah like zina, theft, and highway robbery, then apostatizes, or incurs that after apostasy, then joins dar al-harb, then comes as a Muslim, all that is forgiven except that he compensates property in theft, and if he incurs blood in highway robbery, he is subject to qisas because what is of the rights of the servants, the apostate is held accountable for it. And if he incurs in highway robbery unintentional killing, the blood money is on his 'aqila if he incurred it before apostasy, and from his wealth if he incurred it after apostasy. And if the hadd of drinking wine or intoxicant becomes incumbent on a Muslim, then he apostatizes, then becomes Muslim before joining dar al-harb, he is not punished for it because kufr prevents the obligation of this hadd initially, so it is not obligatory on the dhimmi and musta'min, so if kufr intervenes after obligation, it prevents its continuity. And if he incurs that while the apostate is imprisoned in the hand of the imam, he is not punished for the hadd of wine and intoxication, and he is punished for other hudud of Allah, and the imam is able to establish this hadd if he is in his hand. If he is not in his hand when he incurs that, then becomes Muslim before joining dar al-harb, that is also forgiven. The ruling of his transactions, properties, felony, and children will come later in the book. And he indicated by his statement 'otherwise killed' that enslavement is not permissible even if he joins dar al-harb because only Islam or sword is legislated for him. And in al-Khaniyya: He is not left on his apostasy by giving jizya, nor by temporary aman, nor by permanent aman, and his enslavement is not permissible after joining dar al-harb as an apostate when Muslims take him as a captive. And enslavement of the female apostate after joining dar al-harb is permissible. Among its rulings is that he has no 'aqila because it is for assistance and he is not assisted. And it was mentioned in the chapter of marriage of the disbeliever the occurrence of separation by apostasy of one of the spouses, and in the prohibitions that he does not marry nor is married, and it will come that he does not inherit from anyone due to loss of religion and guardianship. So it became clear that apostasy is more severe than original kufr in this world and the Hereafter. And he unconditionally mentioned killing, so it includes free and slave, so the authority to kill the apostate slave is with the imam, not the master, due to the generality of texts. And in al-Walwaljiyya: If he sells his apostate male slave or female slave, it is permissible, and apostasy is a defect because he is owned by him, so his sale is permissible, and for the slave it necessitates the entitlement to kill him, so it is a defect, and the apostasy of the female slave denies the purchaser the benefit of intercourse, so it is also a defect. And in Sharh al-Majma' citing al-Haqa'iq: He is not to be sat with, nor eaten with, nor is he to be transacted with. And it is a condition for the permissibility of killing the apostate that his Islam is not by way of following, so said in al-Bada'i: A child whose parents are Muslims, so his Islam is ruled by following them, then he reaches puberty as a disbeliever and no verbal affirmation is heard from him after puberty, he is not killed due to absence of apostasy from him, for it is a name for denial after prior affirmation, and no affirmation occurred from him after puberty, so if he affirms Islam then apostatizes, he is killed, but in the first case he is imprisoned because he had the ruling of Islam before its realization, and Allah knows best. Then it is not hidden that all this is concerning other than what is demanded to be fulfilled after Islam like rights of the servants and making up for the prayer and fasting he left.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq detailing the rulings of apostates. It opens by stating that all hudud crimes committed by a person while he was a harbi (non-Muslim in dar al-harb) are forgiven upon his acceptance of Islam, because a harbi is not held accountable for past deeds. It then addresses the case of a Muslim who commits a hadd crime (like zina, theft, highway robbery) then apostatizes, goes to dar al-harb, and later returns as Muslim: these crimes are also forgiven, except that he must compensate for stolen property (damān) and is subject to qisas for murder/homicide because these are rights of people. For unintentional killing during highway robbery, the diya is on his 'āqila if the crime was before apostasy, but from his own wealth if after apostasy. The hadd for drinking is dropped if apostasy occurs because kufr prevents the obligation of such hudud from the start (as with dhimmis and musta'mins), and even if the hadd was already wajib, apostasy obliterates it. However, if the apostate is in the imam's custody, the imam can still execute the hadd for drinking if it was committed before custody. The passage then discusses other rules: a male apostate cannot be enslaved but a female can after joining dar al-harb; the apostate has no 'āqila (group responsible for diya) because he is not entitled to assistance; apostasy severs marriage, prohibits marriage, and denies inheritance. Apostasy is worse than original kufr because it is a rejection after affirmation. The condition for killing an apostate is that he must have been a Muslim by his own affirmation, not just by following parents—a child who reached puberty as a disbeliever without ever affirming Islam is not considered an apostate and is not killed, but is imprisoned. Finally, these rulings exclude the case of pending debts or missed acts of worship that must be fulfilled after Islam.

Key Terms
ردة (riddah): Apostasy from Islam, which is a crime punishable by death in Hanafi law if proven before a judge.
حربي (harbī): A non-Muslim who is not under a pact (dhimma or aman) and resides in dar al-harb, with whom a state of war exists.
عاقلة (ʻāqilah): The group of paternal relatives who collectively pay diyah (blood money) for unintentional killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason that a harbi is not held accountable after Islam for past hudud?
A) Because he was ignorant of the law.
B) Because he was under no Islamic jurisdiction at the time.
C) Because repentance erases all sins.
D) Because the hudud are only for Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that hudud for rights of Allah are dropped when a person leaves Islamic jurisdiction, but rights of people such as property and blood money survive.

Apostasy and the Obligation of Qisas and Diya: Rights of People vs Rights of Allah
Explains the survival of rights of people (qisas, diya, property) after apostasy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between rights of Allah and rights of people in the context of apostasy, and apply the rules for qisas and diya for crimes committed before or after apostasy.

Core Idea
Rights of people (huquq al-‘ibad) survive apostasy, while rights of Allah (huquq Allah) are dropped when the apostate leaves Islamic jurisdiction.

This lesson focuses on the critical distinction between two categories of legal obligations in Islamic law: rights of Allah and rights of people. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that while hudud (penalties for theft, zina, etc.) are forgiven upon apostasy and return, the obligation of qisas (retaliation) for murder and diya (blood money) for unintentional killing remain. Additionally, the timing of the crime—before or after apostasy—affects who pays the diya: the 'aqila or the apostate's own wealth.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of obligations
Rights of Allah (huquq Allah) include hudud penalties. Rights of people (huquq al-‘ibad) include qisas, property, and diya.
2
Apply to apostasy scenario
When an apostate returns to Islam after joining dar al-harb, rights of Allah are forgiven, but rights of people remain enforceable.
Property theft must be compensated (damān).
3
Differentiate between intentional and unintentional killing
Intentional killing requires qisas (retaliation) which is a right of the victim's family. Unintentional killing requires diya (blood money).
4
Note the timing effect on diya
If the unintentional killing occurred before apostasy, diya is on the 'aqila (agnatic group). If after apostasy, it is from the apostate's own wealth.
The apostate has no 'aqila because he is not entitled to assistance.
5
Conclusion
The survival of rights of people underscores that apostasy does not absolve inter-personal liabilities.

Source Text

العبد المرتد للإمام لا للمولى لإطلاق النصوص وفي الولوالجية : إذا باع عبده المرتد أو أمته المرتدة جاز والردة عيب لأنه مملوك له فيجوز بيعه وفي حق العبد يوجب استحقاق القتل عليه فيكون عيباً وردة الأمة تفوّت على المشتري منفعة الوطء فيكون عيباً أيضاً اهـ. وفي شرح المجمع معزياً إلى الحقائق : ولا تجالس ولا تواكل ولا تباع اهـ. ويشترط في جواز قتل المرتد أن لا يكون إسلامه بطريق التبعية ولذا قال في البدائع : صبي أبواه مسلمان حتى حكم بإسلامه تبعاً لأبويه فبلغ كافراً ولم يسمع منه إقرار باللسان بعد البلوغ لا يقتل لانعدام الردة منه إذ هي اسم للتكذيب بعد سابقة التصديق ولم يوجد منه التصديق بعد البلوغ حتى لو أقر بالإسلام ثم ارتد يقتل ولكنه في الأولى يحبس لأنه كان له حكم الإسلام قبل تحقيقه والله أعلم. ثم لا يخفى أن هذا كله في غير الذي يطالب بأدائه بعد الإسلام كحقوق العباد وقضاء ما تركه من صلاة وصيام .
The book of Siyar / Chapter of rulings of apostates. All that is forgiven because it afflicted him while he was a harbi in dar al-harb, and the harbi is not held accountable after Islam for what afflicted him while being a combatant. Whatever a Muslim incurs of the hudud of Allah like zina, theft, and highway robbery, then apostatizes, or incurs that after apostasy, then joins dar al-harb, then comes as a Muslim, all that is forgiven except that he compensates property in theft, and if he incurs blood in highway robbery, he is subject to qisas because what is of the rights of the servants, the apostate is held accountable for it. And if he incurs in highway robbery unintentional killing, the blood money is on his 'aqila if he incurred it before apostasy, and from his wealth if he incurred it after apostasy. And if the hadd of drinking wine or intoxicant becomes incumbent on a Muslim, then he apostatizes, then becomes Muslim before joining dar al-harb, he is not punished for it because kufr prevents the obligation of this hadd initially, so it is not obligatory on the dhimmi and musta'min, so if kufr intervenes after obligation, it prevents its continuity. And if he incurs that while the apostate is imprisoned in the hand of the imam, he is not punished for the hadd of wine and intoxication, and he is punished for other hudud of Allah, and the imam is able to establish this hadd if he is in his hand. If he is not in his hand when he incurs that, then becomes Muslim before joining dar al-harb, that is also forgiven. The ruling of his transactions, properties, felony, and children will come later in the book. And he indicated by his statement 'otherwise killed' that enslavement is not permissible even if he joins dar al-harb because only Islam or sword is legislated for him. And in al-Khaniyya: He is not left on his apostasy by giving jizya, nor by temporary aman, nor by permanent aman, and his enslavement is not permissible after joining dar al-harb as an apostate when Muslims take him as a captive. And enslavement of the female apostate after joining dar al-harb is permissible. Among its rulings is that he has no 'aqila because it is for assistance and he is not assisted. And it was mentioned in the chapter of marriage of the disbeliever the occurrence of separation by apostasy of one of the spouses, and in the prohibitions that he does not marry nor is married, and it will come that he does not inherit from anyone due to loss of religion and guardianship. So it became clear that apostasy is more severe than original kufr in this world and the Hereafter. And he unconditionally mentioned killing, so it includes free and slave, so the authority to kill the apostate slave is with the imam, not the master, due to the generality of texts. And in al-Walwaljiyya: If he sells his apostate male slave or female slave, it is permissible, and apostasy is a defect because he is owned by him, so his sale is permissible, and for the slave it necessitates the entitlement to kill him, so it is a defect, and the apostasy of the female slave denies the purchaser the benefit of intercourse, so it is also a defect. And in Sharh al-Majma' citing al-Haqa'iq: He is not to be sat with, nor eaten with, nor is he to be transacted with. And it is a condition for the permissibility of killing the apostate that his Islam is not by way of following, so said in al-Bada'i: A child whose parents are Muslims, so his Islam is ruled by following them, then he reaches puberty as a disbeliever and no verbal affirmation is heard from him after puberty, he is not killed due to absence of apostasy from him, for it is a name for denial after prior affirmation, and no affirmation occurred from him after puberty, so if he affirms Islam then apostatizes, he is killed, but in the first case he is imprisoned because he had the ruling of Islam before its realization, and Allah knows best. Then it is not hidden that all this is concerning other than what is demanded to be fulfilled after Islam like rights of the servants and making up for the prayer and fasting he left.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq detailing the rulings of apostates. It opens by stating that all hudud crimes committed by a person while he was a harbi (non-Muslim in dar al-harb) are forgiven upon his acceptance of Islam, because a harbi is not held accountable for past deeds. It then addresses the case of a Muslim who commits a hadd crime (like zina, theft, highway robbery) then apostatizes, goes to dar al-harb, and later returns as Muslim: these crimes are also forgiven, except that he must compensate for stolen property (damān) and is subject to qisas for murder/homicide because these are rights of people. For unintentional killing during highway robbery, the diya is on his 'āqila if the crime was before apostasy, but from his own wealth if after apostasy. The hadd for drinking is dropped if apostasy occurs because kufr prevents the obligation of such hudud from the start (as with dhimmis and musta'mins), and even if the hadd was already wajib, apostasy obliterates it. However, if the apostate is in the imam's custody, the imam can still execute the hadd for drinking if it was committed before custody. The passage then discusses other rules: a male apostate cannot be enslaved but a female can after joining dar al-harb; the apostate has no 'āqila (group responsible for diya) because he is not entitled to assistance; apostasy severs marriage, prohibits marriage, and denies inheritance. Apostasy is worse than original kufr because it is a rejection after affirmation. The condition for killing an apostate is that he must have been a Muslim by his own affirmation, not just by following parents—a child who reached puberty as a disbeliever without ever affirming Islam is not considered an apostate and is not killed, but is imprisoned. Finally, these rulings exclude the case of pending debts or missed acts of worship that must be fulfilled after Islam.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for intentional killing or injury, a right of the victim's family.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid for unintentional killing or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an apostate returns to Islam, which of the following obligations is NOT forgiven?
A) Hadd of theft (cutting of hand).
B) Hadd of zina.
C) Property compensation (damān).
D) Hadd of drinking.

Key Takeaway
Rights of people (qisas, diya, property) survive apostasy and are enforceable after the apostate returns to Islam, unlike hudud which are forgiven.
