Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Apostasy and the Status of the Apostate: Enslavement, 'Aqila, and Conditions for Capital Punishment
Explains additional rules on enslavement, 'aqila, and the condition of prior affirmation for capital punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules on enslavement of apostates, the absence of 'aqila, and the condition that capital punishment requires the apostate to have been a Muslim by his own affirmation.

Core Idea
A male apostate cannot be enslaved; a female can; the apostate has no 'aqila; and only a person who affirmed Islam and then denied it can be executed.

This lesson covers additional rulings specific to the apostate's status. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that a male apostate cannot be enslaved even after joining dar al-harb—he must be given the choice of Islam or death. A female apostate, however, can be enslaved. Additionally, the apostate has no 'aqila (agnatic group responsible for blood money) because he is not entitled to assistance. Finally, the passage discusses a critical condition: a child of Muslim parents who reaches puberty as a disbeliever without verbally affirming Islam is not considered an apostate and is not killed, but imprisoned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on enslavement
The text states: 'لا يجوز استرقاقه' (enslavement is not permissible) for a male apostate, even if he joins dar al-harb. For a female, it is permissible.
Rationale: only Islam or sword is legislated for the male apostate.
2
Note the absence of 'aqila
The apostate has no 'aqila because the 'aqila is for mutual assistance, and he is not assisted.
This affects diya payment as seen in the previous lesson.
3
Understand the condition for capital punishment
Killing the apostate is only permissible if his Islam was based on his own affirmation (iqrar), not by mere following (taba'iyya) of parents.
A child who inherits Islam from parents but never personally affirms is not an apostate if he later disbelieves.
4
Apply the condition
If such a person reaches puberty as a disbeliever, he is not killed because there was no prior affirmation to deny. He is imprisoned.
If he later affirms Islam and then apostatizes, he is killed.
5
Conclusion
These rulings highlight that apostasy is treated severely, but with careful conditions that protect those who never truly affirmed Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير/ باب أحكام المرتدين
فذلك كله موضوع عنه لأنه أصابه وهو حربي في دار الحرب والحربي لا يؤاخذ بعد الإسلام بما كان أصابه حال كونه محارباً. وما أصاب المسلم من حدود الله تعالى كالزنا والسرقة وقطع الطريق ثم ارتد أو أصاب ذلك بعد الردة ثم لحق بدار الحرب ثم جاء مسلماً فكل ذلك يكون موضوعاً عنه إلا أنه يضمن المال في السرقة، وإذا أصاب دماً في الطريق كان عليه القصاص لأن ما كان من حقوق العباد كان المرتد مأخوذاً بذلك، وما أصاب في قطع الطريق من القتل خطأ ففيه الدية على عاقلته إن أصابه قبل الردة، وفي ماله إن أصابه بعد الردة، وإن وجب على المسلم حد الشرب من الخمر أو المسكر ثم ارتد ثم أسلم قبل اللحوق بدار الحرب فإنه لا يؤاخذ بذلك لأن الكفر يمنع وجوب هذا الحد ابتداء حتى لا يجب على الذمي والمستأمن فإذا اعترض الكفر بعد الوجوب يمنع البقاء، وإن أصاب ذلك والمرتد محبوس في يد الإمام فإنه لا يؤاخذ بحد الخمر والسكر وهو مؤاخذ بما سوى ذلك من حدود الله تعالى، ويتمكن الإمام من إقامة هذا الحد إذا كان في يده، فإن لم يكن في يده حين أصاب ذلك ثم أسلم قبل اللحوق بدار الحرب فذلك موضوع عنه أيضاً اهـ. وسيأتي حكم تصرفاته وأملاكه وجنايته وأولاده في الكتاب. وأشار بقوله وإلا قتل إلى أنه لا يجوز استرقاقه وإن لحق بدار الحرب لأنه لم يشرع فيه إلا الإسلام أو السيف. وفي الخانية : لا يترك على ردته بإعطاء الجزية ولا بأمان موقت ولا بأمان مؤبد ولا يجوز استرقاقه بعد اللحاق مرتداً إذا أخذه المسلمون أسيراً، ويجوز استرقاق المرتدة بعد اللحاق .اهـ. ومن أحكامه أنه لا عاقلة له لأنها للمعونة وهو يعاون؛ كذا في البدائع. وقد مضى في باب نكاح الكافر وقوع الفرقة بردة أحد الزوجين وفي المحرمات أنه لا ينكح ولا ينكح وسيأتي أنه لا يرث من أحد لانعدام الملة والولاية فقد ظهر أن الردة أفحش من الكفر الأصلي في الدنيا والآخرة وأطلق في القتل فشمل الحر والعبد فولاية قتل Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq detailing the rulings of apostates. It opens by stating that all hudud crimes committed by a person while he was a harbi (non-Muslim in dar al-harb) are forgiven upon his acceptance of Islam, because a harbi is not held accountable for past deeds. For unintentional killing during highway robbery, the diya is on his 'āqila if the crime was before apostasy, but from his own wealth if after apostasy. The hadd for drinking is dropped if apostasy occurs because kufr prevents the obligation of such hudud from the start (as with dhimmis and musta'mins), and even if the hadd was already wajib, apostasy obliterates it. However, if the apostate is in the imam's custody, the imam can still execute the hadd for drinking if it was committed before custody. Finally, these rulings exclude the case of pending debts or missed acts of worship that must be fulfilled after Islam.

Key Terms
تبعية (taba‘iyyah): Following; a legal status derived from another, e.g., a child is Muslim by following his parents.
استرقاق (istirqāq): Enslavement; taking a captive as a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, a male apostate who joins dar al-harb and is captured by Muslims:
A) Must be given a choice between Islam and death; enslavement is not permitted.
B) Can be enslaved like any other captive.
C) Must be released if he pays jizya.
D) Is allowed to remain in dar al-harb under a temporary aman.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has precise conditions for apostasy: capital punishment requires personal prior affirmation of faith, male apostates cannot be enslaved, and they have no 'aqila.
